Current Commentary

Questioning the National Graduation Examination

Recently, education authorities have advocated for a national graduation examination. The idea is that the examination system embodies Dr. Sun Yat-sen's intention for examinations and is a major policy promulgated by the nation to promote teaching efficiency, select true talent, and raise cultural standards. Provinces such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, Anhui, as well as the two cities of Beijing and Shanghai, are all preparing to implement it. However, we believe that this proposal is still open to debate.

We are, of course, absolutely in favor of strict education. In the past twenty years, China has lacked a clear educational direction. Today, we imitate the Japanese system, and tomorrow, we copy the superficial aspects of Europe and America, treating education as a trivial matter and using young people as test subjects. Since the September 18th Incident, the decline and laxity in education have continued as before. If we do not rectify this, the future of our nation and people will truly be doomed.

However, strictness should not be limited to examinations alone, especially not to a superficial national examination. The re-establishment of educational principles, the reorganization of educational administration, and even the transformation of the political and social environment are all extremely urgent and important. In other words, strictness should not be limited to the students. Educational authorities and society as a whole should exercise strict self-discipline. The national crisis since September 18th is the result of twenty years of poor politics and education. Therefore, education after September 18th should strive to be different from education before September 18th. This difference does not lie solely with the students, especially not with the national examination. We should focus on extremely strict daily training. Examination results are not necessarily a reliable indicator of educational achievement.

Those who advocate for the national examination today say it will promote teaching efficiency, select true talent, and raise cultural standards. However, based on our observations, we remain doubtful. Teaching efficiency depends on the entire educational system, the entire social environment, and the quality of school authorities, not on a prize-like examination, especially not on a "imperial examination-style" national examination. This is self-evident. If the national examination is meant to rigorously assess students' achievements, then the rigorous examinations within schools should be able to fulfill this task. If the school's examinations are deemed unreliable, how can we entrust the schools with the important responsibility of training and educating young people? If the school authorities are not trusted, how can we trust those who administer the national examination?

Furthermore, regarding the selection of true talent, so-called "true talent" is not necessarily produced through selection. Moreover, how many of today's administrative officials and educational authorities were actually selected through proper procedures? In recent years, the Examination Yuan has held grand examinations, but many of those who topped the lists have yet to be employed, and some of those who have been employed have been found guilty of corruption. Therefore, the national examination's selection of true talent is not necessarily reliable. As for raising cultural standards, prize-like competition can foster a desire for advancement and increase the pursuit of wealth and power. The evils of the imperial examination era stemmed from this. We dare not believe that it can raise cultural standards.

What is especially worth discussing is that in remote counties and impoverished families, the burden of school fees is already extremely difficult to bear. How can they withstand the added burden of travel expenses? As a result, the national examination will only benefit the children of wealthy families, while those from impoverished families will likely be excluded, which may violate the principles of education.

In short, we are absolutely in favor of strict education today. However, strictness lies in the entire educational policy and the entire educational system, both of which should be re-established. Today is an extraordinary period, and we should have education appropriate for this extraordinary period. We have stated this point before.

US-Japan Talks Involve Far East Issues

Roosevelt劝 Advised Japan to Uphold Arms Reduction

Ishii Requests Instructions from the Tokyo Government

(Washington) President Roosevelt had a long conversation with Japanese representative Ishii. Roosevelt stated that he was very interested and satisfied with his talks with the Japanese representative, which related to the entire range of world issues. It is reported that the talks took place in a very amicable atmosphere, but the discussion of various world issues was limited to theoretical and general terms. Therefore, the talks did not result in any concrete agreements. When Ishii mentioned "Manchukuo," Roosevelt maintained a general attitude and did not want to engage in concrete discussions. Consequently, the Sino-Japanese issue was not addressed. Ishii plans to meet with Roosevelt again before his departure. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

(Washington) During last night's conversation between Japanese representative Viscount Ishii and Roosevelt, Roosevelt requested that Ishii relay to the Tokyo government a change in its stance on the arms reduction conference. Ishii agreed to convey this message to Tokyo. Roosevelt stated that he would schedule another meeting with Ishii once the reply from Tokyo reached Washington. The questions raised by the United States will be telegraphed to the Japanese government by the Japanese representative. Tokyo will respond immediately after receiving the telegram. The reply from the Japanese representative arrived around noon today. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

(Tokyo) Regarding the first meeting between the US President and Japanese representative Ishii, according to reports received by the Foreign Ministry, the US President emphasized the necessity of US-Japan cooperation and proposed two points: in order to ensure the success of the economic conference in the short term, he hoped for Japan's maximum support and cooperation; in order to ensure the success of the conference, the agenda should be limited and the agenda items of the preparatory committee should be removed. Although there are no reports yet regarding the progress of the second meeting, it appears to have focused on the issue of arms reduction. Opinions were exchanged on issues such as peace guarantees and the Far East. Judging from the impressions of the first meeting, the US President does not seem to be bound by Hoover's or Stimson's policies. (Dentsu dispatch, 27th)

Their opinions are as follows: (1) The name "National Defense Corps" should be retained; (2) The National Defense Corps should maintain its independence and not be incorporated into the local army; (3) The tasks should be clearly defined; (4) The number of regular corps soldiers should be set at a maximum; (5) No additional burdens should be placed on the people beyond the original funding; (6) An ordinance for reorganizing the National Defense Corps should be established first, and the existing National Defense Corps should be reorganized before the National Defense Corps Law is finalized. These opinions have been submitted to the central government for approval. (Special dispatch, 27th)

Important Weapon in Economic Warfare

The United States Decides to Formally Abandon the Gold Standard - Congress Submits a Bill at the President's Request to Change the Monetary System Basis of the Past Eighty Years - The Purpose of this Move is to Consolidate the Currency with an Artificial Standard to Make it Easier for Debtor Countries to Cope with Debt Repayments

(Washington) According to today's news, the United States will legislate to abandon the gold standard. (Reuters dispatch, 26th)

(Washington) Today, both the Senate and the House of Representatives simultaneously submitted a bill to abolish the gold standard at the direct request of the US President. The gold standard has been the basis of the American monetary system for nearly 80 years since its adoption in 1853. Although it was abolished twice during the Civil War and in 1893, it was gradually restored. The gold standard law that is now sought to be abolished was re-enacted in 1900, stipulating that the gold dollar should contain 25.8 grains of gold with a fineness of 90 percent, and that all currencies should conform to this standard value, with the Ministry of Finance responsible for maintaining it. If this is passed by Congress and abolished, it means that thereafter, all American currency will no longer be backed by gold, but by the national wealth. Therefore, the nature of this move is not to inflate the currency, but to replace the gold standard with an artificial standard, making all American currency "legal tender." Currently, currencies in the United States, such as silver certificates, national bank notes, Federal Reserve notes, and Federal Reserve bank notes, are commonly used in the market, but in legal terms, they are not "legal tender." When repaying public and private debts, anyone can refuse to accept them and demand payment in gold. This also has no relation to silver. Therefore, the hopes of silver-producing states to re-establish bimetallism have also suffered a serious blow. Senator Fletcher proposed the bill in the Senate today, and Representative Steagall proposed it in the House of Representatives. Steagall explained the effects of the bill: (1) All American currency will henceforth be "legal tender" for the repayment of public and private debts; (2) Foreign war debts owed to the United States will automatically decrease; (3) Banknotes will not need to be redeemed for gold; (4) All future federal government bonds can abolish the gold repayment clause; (5) The government will be able to cope with any international exchange rate situation with ease. Therefore, the purpose of this move is to base the American currency on an artificial standard, so that its value can rise and fall at any time according to international exchange conditions, becoming an important weapon in economic warfare with other countries. Therefore, the leaders of both houses of Congress predict that although this bill will cause the most intense debate in decades, it will ultimately be passed. (National News Agency dispatch, 26th)

(Washington) Representative Steagall, Chairman of the House Banking Committee, today introduced a bill in the House to abolish the gold standard, stating that after the bill is passed, the United States' debtor countries can repay their war debts in any currency commonly used in the United States. The introduction of this bill was at the request of the US President. Steagall said when introducing the bill that it would allow the United States to escape the obstacles of the gold standard. This proposal, together with the proposals of the administrative authorities, is part of President Roosevelt's emergency relief program. This bill can make it unnecessary for the US President to devalue the gold dollar based on the currency inflation clause of the rural relief law. The public sees this as giving the President absolutely free rein, another step in coping with the World Economic Conference. The State Department is confident that this bill will be passed by Congress, lowering the price of the US dollar in international exchange rates, so that the United States can consolidate its currency with a relatively lower standard. However, New York bankers believe that this bill is merely intended to make the de facto situation conform to the law and to clarify the abnormal situation arising from the current gold clause involving hundreds of billions of US dollars in public and private debt. Treasury Secretary Woodin stated that some people may have doubts about the legal status of debtors and creditors regarding repayment in gold. The purpose of this bill is to eliminate this doubt. The bill will add an amendment to the Rural Relief Act, stating that all coins and currencies already minted or issued in the United States, including Federal Reserve notes, Federal Reserve Bank and National Banking Association banknotes, are legal tender for the repayment of public and private debts, as well as national and local taxes. After the proposal to repay war debts with paper money was introduced, bonds rose by as much as 1 to 9 British pounds, and gold mine stocks were very popular. Former Treasury Secretary Glass, the originator of the Federal Reserve System, expressed his opinion today, saying that any move to overturn the gold clause contained in the current contracts will be deemed unconstitutional by the US Supreme Court. (Reuters dispatch, 26th)

(Tokyo) After the news of the new US bill to abolish the gold standard spread, the exchange rate of the Japanese yen against the US dollar rose by half a British pound today, making 100 Japanese yen worth 24 and 1/16 US dollars. There was no change in the exchange rate against the British pound. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

It stated that the Red bandits attacking the Yongxi line approached our army within 200-300 meters and then released smoke bombs. When our officers and soldiers smelled it, they felt cold all over. Investigation revealed that when the smoke bombs exploded, there was a bang, and only thick yellow smoke was seen. After about tens of seconds, breathing felt like sulfuric acid and a pungent taste. Those affected sneezed and felt a slight chill on their bodies, which soon recovered. The casings of the bombs were collected and studied and found to be purely homemade, wrapped in tinplate, shaped like a round one-and-a-half-pound water bottle. The bandits who attacked this time were from Ye Jianying's unit, commanding under the name of the Southeast Operations Political Affairs Committee of the Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army, with about 3,000 people. There were ventilation holes all over the bombs, but how they were thrown is currently unclear. After the Seventh and Eighth Divisions enter Jiangxi, a part of the teaching division will be transferred from the province to take over the defense of the Chaoshan area. In addition, since the Communist bandits in western Jiangxi and other places were suppressed by the majority of the Hunan army, the bandits have scattered in all directions. The Guangdong authorities have been reported to have ordered two regiments of the North River defense forces to go to the city gate of Renhua for strict defense. As for Chen Jitang, since he was appointed by the Central Government as the Commander-in-Chief of the bandit suppression in the five provinces of Hunan, Jiangxi, Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian, he has indeed been preparing to take office. He has been busy preparing for departure for days, and has been actively carrying out preparations for the procurement of military supplies, the organization of the headquarters, and transportation. Even the plaque of the Commander-in-Chief of the bandit suppression in the five provinces is being manufactured. Judging from this, Chen's taking the post of Commander-in-Chief of bandit suppression should not change. (22nd)

Wuhan Textile Mill

Labor Dispute Still Difficult to Resolve

Unemployed Workers from Zhenhuan Petition the Headquarters

Provincial Party Department Decides to Order the Factory to Resume Work Immediatley

Hankou Correspondence: The closure of the Wuchang Zhenhuan Textile Mill due to losses has caused a labor dispute. For days, the workers have been appealing to various agencies, but there has been no way to resolve it. On the 24th, Hu Peichu, a supervisor of the Textile Industry Union, led more than 40 worker representatives to the Construction Department to petition again, where they were received by Zhang Zhengxing, who said that he had sent a special official, Hu Bao, to contact the factory and asked them to endure and wait patiently for a resolution. The next day, the worker representatives went to the Party and Government Committee of the Headquarters to petition again, where they were received by Chen Juewu. The representatives handed over a petition, which stated, "The Zhenhuan Textile Mill suddenly closed on the 22nd, without prior approval from the government or advance notice to the workers. This was a bolt from the blue, leaving the workers on the brink of despair. The recession in the textile industry in our country is not limited to Wuchang, nor just the Zhenhuan Mill. It is setting a precedent to suddenly leave more than 3,000 workers unemployed at a time of national crisis. What is their intention? For the sake of our livelihoods and the future of the national economy, the workers have no choice but to appeal to the General, who saves the country and the people, to strictly order the company to resume work immediately, so as to prevent the workers from becoming starving corpses." Chen said that the facts were not yet clear and needed to be investigated and verified. The worker representatives withdrew without getting what they wanted. The Textile Workers' Union, after repeated negotiations, received no concrete response from the factory, and the military and political authorities had no mediation measures. All the workers were extremely angry. If this continued, it was feared that the workers would expand the disturbance due to their urgent need for a livelihood, and it would be difficult to bear this heavy responsibility. Therefore, on the 25th, they submitted requests to various military and political agencies for instructions. That day happened to be the regular meeting of the Provincial Party Department. All the members sympathized with the workers. After deliberation, it was decided to order the Zhenhuan Textile Mill to resume operations immediately to maintain the workers' livelihoods and to recommend Yang Zaichun, a member, to be responsible for mediation together with a member appointed by the Provincial Government. The Provincial Government also scheduled a discussion at the regular meeting on the 26th. During this labor dispute, more than 3,000 workers have been running around appealing, without overstepping their bounds, which has garnered much sympathy from society. The authorities are also paying close attention. However, the attitude of the factory is quite firm, and it is not yet known whether there will be a satisfactory outcome. Investigation revealed that the factory's capital is 1.3 million yuan and has more than 3,000 workers. According to the factory, it has lost more than 700,000 yuan. If this is not an exaggeration, then resuming work will not be easy. As for other textile mills, apart from the Yuhua Mill, which has a capital of 5 million yuan, 3 million yuan in public reserve and surplus, and only 4,000 workers, which can still maintain the status quo, the Minsheng Mill, with a capital of 400,000 yuan and 3,000 workers, can also barely maintain after reducing wages. However, the First Textile Mill is also surrounded by crises. The mill has a capital of approximately 4 million yuan and more than 9,000 workers. Although it is managed by Chinese, it has been mortgaged to the foreign firm Anley & Ying, with a mortgage of 3 million taels. In reality, it is no longer owned by Chinese. In recent years, the mill has lost more than 1.3 million yuan and is also brewing a suspension of operations. However, the factory authorities are currently pursuing a loan of 2 million yuan from Sassoon & Company. If this can be achieved, they can continue to operate. Otherwise, they will inevitably have to suspend operations, and more than 9,000 workers will again have no recourse. (25th)

Japanese Aviation Department Plans

Air Defense Exercises This Autumn

Reorganizing the Combined Fleet into a Standing Fleet — American-Made New Airship Guards the Pacific Coast

According to the Osaka Asahi Shimbun on May 21st, the Army Aviation Headquarters has been planning exercises since last summer. The Second Destroyer Division is attached to the Combined Fleet, and other ships such as Irimiya, Naruto, Tsurumi, and Notoro are also included.

Jieyang Youmazhashan Township

A Major Massacre Occurs

Two Clans Clash, Resulting in Over Twenty Casualties

County Government, Upon Hearing the News, Insists on Strict Handling

Shantou Correspondence: The Mianhu District of Jieyang County borders Punin and Fengshun counties, approximately forty miles from Jieyang City. Due to obstructed transportation, various clans reside in separate villages and have historically been on bad terms. There exist divisions such as large villages versus small villages, major clans versus minor clans, powerful lineages versus weak lineages, and "red" factions versus "white" factions. Minor issues often escalate into revenge killings and violent clashes. In the past, events such as the conflict between Fengshun’s Pucang and Yangxia villages, and Punin’s Nigou and Baxiang villages, originated from extremely minor incidents, leading to the tragic burning of villages and killing of people. Those who speak of these past events still feel lingering fear. On the ninth of this month, Lin Zaifa of Tonghang, relying on his large clan population (approximately 16,000 men), cut down longan trees belonging to the Huang clan of the neighboring Youmazhashan village for firewood. When the Huang clan attempted to stop him, Lin refused and responded with harsh words, leading to a verbal dispute that escalated into a physical fight. Determining right from wrong was difficult. After being beaten, Lin Zaifa informed his father and clansmen. On the eleventh, the villagers gathered with weapons and attacked Youmazhashan village, killing many members of the Huang clan and imprisoning women in one location. They looted extensively, taking away cattle and clothing. The Huang clan only had four hundred men, a significantly smaller force compared to the Lin clan, and therefore dared not resist. Local gentry, seeing the unfavorable situation, stepped in to mediate. However, the Lin clan was stubborn, demanding a fine of five hundred yuan from the Huang clan. The Huang clan refused to submit. On the thirteenth, more than thirty women went to the county government to seek assistance and request protection. Upon learning that the Huang clan had filed a complaint with the authorities, the Lin clan simultaneously mobilized strong men and prepared weapons, and reported to the Mianhu Security Guard platoon, claiming that bandits were plotting to attack Tonghang from villages such as Youmazhashan Fengkezhai. The Security Guard platoon believed this to be true and, armed with guns and ammunition, entered Youmazhashan village on the morning of the fourteenth, barging into homes and firing indiscriminately, discharging thousands of bullets, resulting in over twenty casualties and the burning of a clan hall and dozens of houses. They also abducted nine people. Lin clan strong men assisted from within, causing great chaos. Subsequently, they proceeded to Fengkezhai to burn and kill, as Fengke, Maqiu, and Liushuipu villages were all part of the White Flag faction. On the fifteenth, the county government dispatched Zhang Cexun leading a Security Guard Brigade to suppress the situation. Court prosecutor Zhang Peiling, along with a clerk, went to the scene to investigate and examine the injuries. On the sixteenth, they further investigated Fengkezhai. On that day, sixty to seventy women refugees from the Huang clan of Youmazhashan rushed to the county government and various branch offices to voice their grievances, with disheveled hair and bare feet, their plight was pitiable. On the seventeenth, County Magistrate Xie Henian personally went to Tonghang village to investigate and detained local gentry Lin Xiangzhen and Lin Huiyan at the brigade headquarters for questioning. It is reported that the Red and White Flag factions have been secretly brewing a major conflict for a long time. The Lin clan Red Flag faction had previously organized a farmers' association before the sixteenth year of the Republic and used special powers to oppress other clans. Later, smaller villages and mixed clans, with the support of the Purification Party and the White Flag faction, retaliated against the Red Flag using the same tactics. Currently, both sides are actively preparing for war and discriminating against each other. The Zhang clan of Puzhaizhai and the Lin clan of Yangxia village are building earthen walls and gun emplacements on the mountaintops in their respective villages, working day and night. The scope of this conflict involves several counties, with major clan divisions arising in various districts and villages. Consequently, people in Jieyang, recalling past events, cannot help but turn pale at the mention of conflict. County gentry Deng Guoliang, Lin Kuichu, Guo Ruifu, and dozens of others are separately mediating in various locations. On the eighteenth, over sixty women refugees from the Huang clan came to Shantou to petition the Eastern District Pacification Commissioner to seek justice and protect the innocent. The county government is paying close attention to this matter. As the military is currently engaged in suppressing bandits in Jiangxi, there is great concern that the conflict will escalate, affecting local security. Therefore, they insist on strict handling to prevent the situation from expanding. It is reported that the mediators are successfully persuading reconciliation in various villages, with good prospects for resolution. (Twenty-third)

Signs of Drought Seen in Chao-Shan This Spring

Rainbow Halo Around the Sun in the Sky

Villagers Pray to Gods for Rain

Shantou Correspondence: On the morning of the nineteenth, the weather in Chao-Shan was exceptionally hot. At eleven o'clock, a slight breeze suddenly arose, and fleeting clouds transformed unpredictably in the sky. People believed that heavy rain was imminent. After a while, the wind calmed, and the scorching sun blazed overhead. Suddenly, a five-colored rainbow halo appeared around the sun, its colors bright and pleasing to the eye, lasting for about half an hour before gradually dissipating. Residents gathered on the streets to look up and admire it, marveling at the spectacle. Superstitious individuals considered it an ominous sign, and rumors spread rapidly. This spring in Chao-Shan has been marked by severe drought. In February, a smallpox epidemic broke out, spreading quickly. Currently, cerebrospinal meningitis is also prevalent and spreading rapidly. One acute form of the disease causes dizziness and drowsiness at the onset, followed by convulsions in the limbs and strained breathing, leading to death in less than two hours. Many children over ten years old in the Western Pass of Chaoan have contracted the disease, and several have died before treatment could be administered. Mangoes, bayberries, lychees, peaches, and plums have already appeared on the market, and cholera and diarrhea are also emerging alongside them. The epidemic is rampant, all due to the arid weather. The drought situation this spring is extremely serious in various counties. The early rice harvest is only about forty percent. Coupled with the continuous lack of rain, the rice leaves have turned dry and yellow. Dabu and other counties have already reported the disaster to the provincial government. In Chaoan and Jieyang counties, rain-prayer ceremonies were held last month. Dozens of benevolent societies, along with five or six hundred Buddhist disciples, carried statues of deities in processions through the streets, kneeling every three steps to prostrate themselves to the sky. On the eighteenth, praying and kneeling groups were also formed in Chaoyang Dahu and other places. In Dabu Sanheba, a rain-requesting drumming team was organized. People carried dozens of large drums, carrying the deities and parading along the streets, beating the drums loudly, resembling thunder. The drummers and the praying procession all wore bamboo hats and inserted banyan tree leaves, a custom passed down through generations. In Meixian, known for its advanced education, a Guanyin-praying team also appeared on the seventeenth. The monasteries and temples in Meixian have a type of nun who does not shave her head, known as a "zhaifu," who specializes in praying on behalf of people to resolve calamities and release the souls of the dead. This spring drought was initiated by zhaifu from the west, carrying Guanyin statues in processions, gathering hundreds of zhaifu from the entire county, all dressed in black skirts and inserting green leaves in their hair, marching in formation. Ignorant and foolish people set up incense tables at their doorways, bowing their heads in prostration, which is truly laughable. (Twenty-third)

Shandong Construction Bureau Dredges Jinan's Famous Springs

Historically Known as the Seventy-Two Springs of Lixia

Willow Catkins and Yellow Flowers Offer Opportunities for Remembrance

Jinan Correspondence: The Jishui River flows underground. Ancient texts claim that the springs of Lixia gush out everywhere, numbering seventy-two. Ancient people said, "The mountains and waters of Lixia are the best in Shandong, and the springs are the best in the world," which is not an exaggeration. However, with the passage of time, except for the well-known major springs, which still have remnants that can be found, the rest have been lost and forgotten. The current provincial government is the former palace of the Ming Dynasty Prince, and there are dozens of springs within its grounds. The most famous ones are the Pearl Spring, White Cloud Spring, Zhuoying Spring, and South Tutu Spring. The Baotu Spring remains one of the famous scenic spots today. Dozens of paces east of Baotu Spring is the former residence of the Song Dynasty female poet Li Qingzhao (now the Provincial Medical School). Famous springs within the residence, such as the Golden Coin Spring, Nenyu Spring, Willow Catkin Spring, and Yellow Flower Spring, also have historical value. Poets and writers often visit to remember her, and whenever they recall the line "Don't say it doesn't break the heart, the curtains roll up in the west wind, the person is thinner than the yellow flower," they linger and are reluctant to leave. The Construction Bureau, in order to renovate Xiaoqing River, has investigated and dredged various famous springs in Jinan to increase the water source, and a total of fifty-three locations have been identified. The names of the springs are as follows: (1) Ancient Jinhu Pool, in the Sumeru Garden of the Fan family at No. 10 South Shuncheng Street. A stone tablet beside the pool is inscribed with the name "Jinli Spring." (2) Huibo Spring, at the entrance of the Fan family's Sumeru Garden, on the south bank of the South Moat, also known as the Pao Ma Spring (Running Horse Spring). (3) Yinsi Spring, below the Dragon King Temple on South Shuncheng Street. The name of the spring is engraved on the door of the Dragon King Temple. (4) Pearl Spring, beside the South Moat behind Banbian Street. This spring is the South Pearl Spring. (5) Pipa Spring, at No. 13, Banbian Street, behind a residential house, beside the moat. (6) Black Tiger Spring, outside the back wall of the Banbian Street County Primary School. This spring can be seen only by entering through the small door at No. 9. (7) Agate Spring, at the entrance of No. 6, Banbian Street, beside the moat. The name of the spring is engraved on a stone incense burner. (8) White Stone Spring, opposite the Agate Spring. There is a stone tablet beside it with the name of the spring inscribed. (9) Ren Spring, in the east courtyard of the Qiao Shaojiu Company on Dongyanwo Street. A large stone to the north of the pond is inscribed with the name of the spring. (10) Ancient Jian Spring, at the east entrance of the Houti Guan Street outside the South Gate, beside the outer moat. A stone tablet in front of Houti Guan Street is inscribed with the name of the spring. (11) Shun Well, on the west side of Shun Well Street. The words "Shun Well Pool" are embedded in the wall north of the pool. (12) Fragrant Spring, at No. 2, Shun Temple Street, in the backyard of the Shun Temple. (13) Mi Zhi Spring, on the north side of Guyi Shi Street, in the backyard of Wanshunxiang. The spring water flows into Jiang Jia Pond. (14) Hui Chi Spring, in the backyard of the dyeing workshop at No. 21, Dongliushui, beside the Five Dragon Pool. (15) Hui Wan Spring, in the backyard of No. 9 Kunming Pond. The name of the spring was obtained through inquiry and is subject to verification. (16) Xuan Qing Spring, at No. 49 Dongliushui, in the backyard of Fa Ji. The name of the spring was obtained through inquiry. (17) Tian Jing Spring, beside the Deshenglou on the east side of Jiang Jia Chi Street, renamed Spring Mirror Spring by residents who call it Jiang Jia Chi. (18) Ancient Hot Spring, at the south end of Dongliushui, on the west side of the road. A stone embedded in the west wall is inscribed with the name of the spring. (19) Central Pearl Spring, in the west courtyard of the Provincial Government. A stone tablet in the pavilion beside the pond is inscribed with the name of the spring. (20) Chu Spring, in the west courtyard inside the Provincial Government's main gate. A stone embedded in the wall bears the name of the spring. (21) North Hibiscus Spring, at No. 25 Daimiao Street. A stone embedded in the wall is inscribed with the name of the spring. (22) Little Prince Mansion Pond, outside the gate of No. 13 Wangfu Chi Street. (23) Hibiscus Spring, in the courtyard of the pharmacy on the west side of Furong Street, commonly known as Hibiscus Pond. (24) Teng Jiao Spring, at No. 14 on the south side of Qifeng Street. A stone embedded in the wall is inscribed with the name of the spring. (25) Luo Yuan Spring, in the Normal School on Yuansi Street. A stone embedded in the wall is inscribed with the name of the spring. (26) Jade Ring Spring, on the west side of Buzheng Si Street. A stone embedded in the wall is inscribed with the name of the spring. (27) Earth Spring, inside the Civil Affairs Department, also known as Jubao Spring. (28) Feng Zhu Pond, inside the main gate of the Civil Affairs Department. The Guangrun Temple inside the Department has a stele that details this spring. (29) Jade Milk Spring, at the foot of the mountain north of the Guangrun Temple in the Civil Affairs Department. A stone tablet is inscribed with the name of the spring. (30) Snow Spring, in the courtyard of No. 43 West Palace Street. A stone tablet in the room east of the pond bears the inscription "Record of Snow Spring." (31) Inexhaustible Spring, in the east courtyard of the Agriculture and Mining Department. (32) North China Pond, inside the second gate of the Agriculture and Mining Department. A stone block beside it is engraved with the name of the spring. (33) Guangfu Spring, in the courtyard of a shop at No. 24 Shuangzhong Temple Street. The spring was discovered by a citizen's investigation.

(34) Xiaogan Spring, inside the gate of No. 9 Dazhi Street. (35) Chou Kang Spring, behind the house at No. 10 Houying Street. (36) Tonghui Spring, in the Jinan Commercial Field, on the north side of the courtyard. A stone tablet is inscribed with the name of the spring. (37) Bridge Spring, inside the Yaowang Temple on Baotu Spring Front Street. There is a stone carving beside it with the name of the spring. (38) Shiwan Spring, inside the gate of No. 24 Weiping Street. The "Record of the Xiaoqing River Near Source Investigation" confirms that it is this spring. According to the Xiaoqing River Investigation Record, it is this spring. (49) Worry-Free Spring, north of the artificial mountain in the Baotu Spring market. The Xiaoqing River Near Source Record identifies it as this spring. (50) Baotu Spring, in front of the Lvzu Pavilion in the Baotu Spring market. There is a stele in the pool with various calligraphic styles of "Paotu Spring," and some write "First Spring." (51) Du Kang Spring, outside the west wall of Baotu Spring on Huacangzi Street. A stone tablet is embedded in the wall, bearing the name "Wang Lu Spring." This spring is a square pond east of Sizhao Tower, but no traces can be found now. Additions: (1) In the east garden behind Woyuan at No. 2, Banbian Street, there is a square pool, each side measuring one zhang and two chi, with a water depth of three chi, but with no name. (Twenty-sixth)

Letter from the Construction Bureau of the Zhejiang Provincial Government

To the Shanghai Shenbao:

Upon investigation, the two articles published in your newspaper on the 24th of this month, "Merchants and People in the Old Quzhou Region of Zhejiang Province Oppose Highway Stock Funds," are largely inconsistent with the facts. The "Provisional Measures for Raising Funds for Road Construction in Various Counties of the Old Quzhou Region of Zhejiang Province" were implemented after a resolution by the Provincial Government Committee. Regarding the methods for raising stock funds, there are two categories: (1) Soliciting donations from wealthy individuals in the local area; (2) Collecting stock funds from the old Quzhou region's bamboo, timber, and charcoal, which are borne by the owners. However, for the convenience of collection, the merchants will first pay the road stock, and then be issued stock certificates. The contributing people can share the benefits, which is different from ordinary donations and taxes. The establishment of the Stock Fund Raising Committee and its branch offices is also different from the nature of setting up checkpoints for levying taxes. If the staff members of the offices are found to be making things difficult, demanding bribes, or embezzling funds, they will be severely punished according to the law once reported. Previously, it was reported that timber merchants in Yongjia hired workers to Qingtai to forcibly release rafts. This Bureau immediately telegraphed the magistrate of Qingtai County to provide proper guidance and to either pay the stock fund or pay a security deposit before allowing the release. If the merchants comply with the regulations, the offices will not detain them without authorization. As for the claim of firing guns as a threat, it is even more of an exaggeration. This road stock is very important for the development of transportation in eastern Zhejiang. All the details are reported to the Provincial Government by this Bureau for review. Deeply concerned that there may be misunderstandings due to rumors, we have sent this letter requesting that you promptly make corrections. Sincerely, Construction Bureau of Zhejiang Provincial Government, May 25th.

Songjiang

News of Zhu Yunting's Suicide

Zhu Yunting from the East Gate was only thirty years old. His father had accumulated an estate worth about six or seven thousand taels of gold through a lifetime of hard work and toil. After his father passed away, Yunting sought to profit from the assets and invested in the Lifeng Cotton Weaving Factory. However, the business was sluggish and suffered some losses. Despite this, Zhu was employed at the factory and rose to become a respectable merchant. He then conceived the idea of building a house and contracted a local contractor for the construction in the winter of the previous year, estimating the cost at over two thousand yuan. While bricks and wood were being transported to his home, a relative saw this and strongly recommended a contractor named Bao. Initially, the construction cost was similar to the previous estimate. Zhu, lured by sweet words, signed a contract with Bao to undertake the construction. Unexpectedly, after the construction started, Bao claimed that the original accounts were missing many items and gradually increased the price. By the time the construction was completed in the winter of the following year, the cost had reached a staggering seven or eight thousand yuan. Moreover, Bao used various means to demand payment urgently. Mr. Zhu, feeling that his inheritance had been exhausted and that he still owed four or five thousand yuan, and suffering repeated irritations, became disillusioned with life. He went to Shanghai the day before yesterday and committed suicide by taking poison at a relative's house. His family reported the incident and claimed the body for burial in Songjiang. He left behind an elderly mother, a wife, and several children, whose livelihoods are now extremely difficult. It is said that Contractor Bao made a profit of three thousand yuan from building Zhu's house, and the person who made the introduction also received a commission of seven hundred yuan. Zhu Yunting's pursuit of vanity and poor judgment led to a tragic end. Commentators lamented his fate.

Wuxi

Two New Judges Added to the County Court

The number of civil and criminal lawsuits in this county is high. The adjudication division of the County Court originally had one president who also served as a substantive judge, and three probationary judges. As these were insufficient, the Ministry of Justice has appointed Pan Jiatian as a trainee judge, who has already arrived at his post. In addition, the Procuratorate originally had two procurators. After Procurator Du Jiasheng was transferred back to Zhenjiang to resume his original post, the cases handled by Procurators Zhou Erkai and Shen Zhaoming were extremely busy. The Higher Procuratorate was petitioned, which in turn petitioned the Ministry of Justice, to appoint Jin Fengao as a procurator, and he is expected to arrive in Wuxi soon.

Xie Dasen Confiscates Enemy Cloth and Punishes

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of this county seized a large quantity of enemy goods cloth at Xie Dasen Gangbu Store the other day. After holding the 30th Committee meeting, it was decided to confiscate all the goods according to Article 11 of the Revised Measures for Suppressing Enemy Goods promulgated by the province, and to punish the store three times the value of the goods.

Zhenjiang

Farmer's Son Kidnapped for Ransom

Recently, bandits in the four rural districts have emerged in an endless stream, and kidnappings for ransom have occurred frequently. Recently, in the Kaowei Toudui area of Dingye Township in the first district, a man named Fang Yuancai, who worked as a farmer, had a decent life and was targeted by bandits. At about 1 a.m. on the 23rd of this month, eight bandits broke down the front door and rushed in, overturning chests and ransacking at will for about an hour. Before leaving, they kidnapped Fang's ten-year-old son, leaving a red paper note that read, "Contact between 7 p.m. and 9 p.m. on the 26th in the Sibaidu area. A 'meeting gift' of 5,000 yuan is required, along with two large boxes of cigarettes. The signal is a hand-held lantern with a green bamboo pole. Only two people are allowed. If there are three, we will open fire and kill." Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to the township head, Ma Yuanqing, who reported it to the district regiment headquarters, which in turn reported it to the Provincial Security Office, requesting that the water and land public security agencies jointly investigate the matter.

Jiangyin

Two Escaped Female Prisoners Recaptured

On March 1 this year, the female prisoners He Chen and others escaped from the county prison. The province issued a wanted order. On the 23rd, the Su-Song Headquarters captured Xu Su, one of the escapees, in Xinan Town, Changzhou (originally sentenced to ten years). The Public Security Bureau was notified and dispatched Inspector Song Renjie to bring her back. Xu Su confessed to the hideout of the remaining escapees. Li Wang, another escapee, was captured at Yuecheng Bridge. Both were escorted to the county for interrogation on the 15th.

Automobile Ticket Sales Collect Charitable Donations

The relief institution requires a large amount of funds for various relief undertakings. The director, Cao Yuanmo, proposed to the Xicheng long-distance automobile company and various small automobile companies to collect a charitable donation of 30 cents per passenger ticket. Gu Haojia contacted the automobile company on the 26th. The company expressed that it was impossible to refuse, but feared that the passengers would object. It was necessary to pass the county political meeting and submit it to the province for approval before allowing the collection. All the small automobile companies were unwilling to comply.

Nantong

Provincial Committee Visits Nantong to Design a Bank Protection Project

Recently, the riverbank in Nantong has been collapsing severely. Local people from all walks of life have gathered to discuss bank protection. It has been decided to appeal to the province for relief and to request the county government to present the following to the provincial government: (1) To promptly send a special commissioner to Nantong to preside over the design of the bank protection project; (2) To approve the appropriation of all the land tax collected this year for road construction for the local bank protection expenses, together with more than 100,000 yuan in land tax collected and continued for bank protection, plus a matching allocation from the provincial treasury, there will be 200,000 yuan, which will be sufficient for the project needs. On the 26th, the provincial government ordered the county government to send Xu Ji, the chief engineer of the Construction Department, to Nantong as soon as possible to preside over the design.

Tragic Bridge Collapse at Changhetan

In Changhetan, in the northern district, there was a religious drama performance. More than 50 men and women were on the wooden bridge over the river, watching. The bridge could not bear the weight and suddenly broke, causing more than 30 people to fall into the water and get injured, and 5 deaths.

Gaoyou

Security Corps Mistakenly Kills Passenger

Li Zufen, head of the Security Corps in the tenth district of the county, is currently responding to the rampant banditry in the district. The other day, he accompanied the police team stationed in the district on patrol in various villages. When they arrived in Zhuzhuang Township, a passenger from Yancheng, Tang Youyin, became frightened when he saw the team approaching and ran away wildly. The team, seeing this, feared that he was not a good person and opened fire to pursue him. Tang Youyin was hit by two bullets and fell to the ground and died. After investigation, it was learned that the deceased was to be married to a Dai family in Zhoujin Township. It was also a tragedy.

Yangzhou

Carpenter Chases Thief and Is Shot Dead

Yin Lancai, a resident of Gu Jia Zhuang in Shao Bo south township, was a carpenter, raised four sons, and had a decent livelihood, which made him the target of petty thieves. Last night, three thieves dug a hole and entered his house, stealing two pieces of salted meat and a bag of powdered noodles. As they were escaping, Lancai and his sons were awakened by the noise. Seeing the situation was unfavorable, the thieves burst out the door. The two younger sons bravely pursued them, chasing them to the Baji Kou highway behind the village, the thieves turned back and struck ferociously, seriously injuring his two sons, one died on the spot, and the other was barely breathing, and his life was in danger.

Local News

Completion of the Shanghai-Chengdu Air Route

Officially Inaugurated on June 1st

Post Office Sells Commemorative Envelopes

The Shanghai-Chengdu line (Shanghai to Chengdu) of the China National Aviation Corporation previously only went to Chongqing. Now the Chongqing to Chengdu section has been scheduled to open on June 1 (yesterday's newspaper mistakenly recorded it as June 8). The entire line has now been completed. The fees for air mail from Shanghai to Chengdu are calculated as two flight zones (each 1,000 miles is a flight zone), namely Shanghai-Hankou as one flight zone and Hankou-Chengdu as another flight zone. In addition to the normal postage, an additional airmail fee of 25 cents per 20 grams or fraction thereof is charged for each flight zone. To commemorate the opening of the Shanghai-Chengdu air route, the Shanghai North Suzhou Road Postal Administration has prepared "Shanghai-Chengdu Air Route Opening Commemorative Envelopes" for sale on Monday, the 29th. The number of these envelopes is very limited. The price is 5 cents each. All mail destined for various locations on the Chongqing-Chengdu air route that is intended to be sent out when the air route opens must be posted on or before Monday, the 29th.

According to the Shanghai Times, Mr. Pond of the China National Aviation Corporation, accompanied by Mr. Baker of the Flying Corps and Mr. Chaplim, the postal officer of this city, flew directly from Shanghai to Chongqing yesterday (the 26th) in a plane of the company, covering a distance of 2,600 kilometers non-stop. After departing from Shanghai in the early morning, they were scheduled to arrive in Chongqing in the late afternoon in order to fly from Chongqing to Chengdu tomorrow (the 28th) for a test flight between Chongqing and Chengdu, and to officially open the route on Thursday (June 1st). The distance between Chongqing and Chengdu is 306 kilometers, while the distance from Shanghai to Chongqing is 2,658 kilometers.

Scheduled Shanghai-Guangdong Air Route

July 1st

A spokesman for the China National Aviation Corporation told reporters from the Aviation News Agency yesterday that in order to open the Shanghai-Guangdong air route, the company had previously sent Nie Kaiyi, deputy director of the flight crew, with radio equipment to various stations along the route to prepare everything. According to the report, the progress is quite smooth. It has been decided to officially open the route on July 1st. There will be daily flights except on Mondays, arriving on the same day, several days earlier than by ship. The airmail rates and ticket prices have not yet been determined, but the airmail fee will probably only be calculated as one air zone, and the one-way ticket price will not exceed 250 yuan.

Aviation Donations for Aircraft

Public Groups Should Be Allowed Freedom

Negotiations with the Aviation Association Prove Ineffective

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, the Ningbo Sojourners' Association in Shanghai's fundraising committee has raised over 96,000 yuan since it began its small-scale fundraising efforts. Recognizing the urgency of the national crisis and to encourage enthusiastic participation in aviation for national salvation, the committee ordered a fighter plane from the British Vickers-Armstrong Company. The general office of the China Aviation Association's fundraising team learned of this and sent Mr. Zhang Xiaoliang to visit Mr. Lin Mianzhai, an officer of the Ningbo Sojourners' Association, at 10:00 AM yesterday. Zhang claimed that the Aviation Association had decided that all aviation donations should be centralized within the Aviation Association, then remitted to the municipal government, which would then purchase the aircraft. He asked why the Ningbo Sojourners' Association was acting independently and requested a clear response that afternoon. Lin replied that aviation for national salvation was a matter of voluntary donation by the public and that public groups should be allowed the freedom to purchase aircraft independently, and he declined the request. It is also reported that the Tianchu MSG Factory also voluntarily donated 100,000 silver dollars for aviation for national salvation, and the Aviation Association's office has repeatedly sent personnel to request the funds, but without success. Negotiations are still underway.

National Goods Factory Association Cables Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters

To Stop the Discount Sale of Enemy Goods

Listing Four Reasons

The Shanghai National Goods Factory Association telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters yesterday, requesting a ban on the auction of enemy goods. The telegram stated, "During the factory representatives' meeting convened by our association on May 25th, Standing Committee member Zhang Zilian proposed that he had previously seen reports in Hangzhou newspapers about a public auction of enemy goods confiscated since the September 18th Incident. Zilian raised objections, citing four reasons: (1) The auction of enemy goods undermines the movement for economic severance with Japan. (2) The auction of enemy goods opens the door for merchants to privately traffic in enemy goods. (3) The auction of enemy goods encourages the public to use enemy goods, stifling their sense of shame and aversion towards the enemy and openly violates the government's order to use domestic goods. (4) The auction of enemy goods will greatly impact the anti-Japanese goods movement in various provinces and cities. Zhejiang's initiation of such action is a loss of Zhejiang's integrity. A letter had already been sent to the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese Association requesting the cancellation of the original proposal. As this matter concerns the violation of the entire plan for economic severance with Japan, our Shanghai member factories should unanimously advocate for a request to the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters to instruct a ban. Please render a public decision." The entire body of representatives resolved, based on Standing Committee member Zhang's proposal, to adopt the following measures: (1) Telegraph the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters to instruct the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese Association to cease the auction of enemy goods. (2) Advise all goods owners to voluntarily burn enemy goods to express their patriotic fervor. (3) Donate the confiscated enemy goods to frontline soldiers. (4) Before the lost territories of the Northeast are recovered, enemy goods should continue to be sealed up. This has been recorded in the minutes. We hereby submit this matter to your office for review, earnestly requesting that you consider the gravity of the national crisis and, after examining the four reasons proposed by Zhang Zilian and the four measures resolved by the representatives' meeting, issue instructions to the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association to halt the proposed auction of Japanese goods, in order to implement the entire plan for economic severance with Japan."

Chinese-Owned Cotton Mills

Yesterday, Continued Labor Reduction

Work to Resume Tomorrow

The Chinese-owned cotton mills have decided to adopt previous measures, reducing labor by 23% and suspending Saturday and Sunday night shifts. Yesterday was the first Saturday. In this city, 28 Chinese-owned cotton mills, including Hengfeng, Shenxin, Yongan, and Puyi, except for Chongxin Cotton Mill at Tanjiadu No. 1, which had not yet reduced labor, and the Jingwei Mingji Cotton Mill at the corner of Yuezhou Road and Gongping Road, which was processing waste cotton and did not suspend work, all 26 remaining mills announced the suspension of work. Workers were scattered in their homes, maintaining good order. Today is Sunday, and the mills continue to suspend work. Work will resume tomorrow, Monday.

Inspection of Concession Factories

Negotiations Progressing Smoothly

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the inspection of concession factories, Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, based on centrally determined principles, has been consulting with Mr. Feixin Dun, the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement, on a resolution. Progress is quite smooth, and it has been decided to continue discussions early next month to achieve a quick resolution. According to sources familiar with the situation, the Municipal Council no longer insists on opposing the Municipal Government's implementation of sovereignty over the inspection of concession factories, as they are well aware that this pertains to China's overall sovereignty and cannot be seized. Therefore, the focus of negotiations is no longer on the issue of sovereignty but on how to ensure the safety of equipment in the factories within the concession and how to conduct inspections. According to Municipal Council sources, it is expected that the outcome of the negotiations will be that the inspection work will be jointly conducted by the Municipal Government and the Municipal Council, with the highest authority belonging to the Municipal Government.

Confirmed…But Not a New Loan

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, in order to replenish funds for resisting Japan and suppressing the communists, the Ministry of Finance, through Vice Minister Zou Lin, recently established a short-term loan of five million yuan with the banking sector in this port. Banking sector officials and responsible persons stated that the loan matter is confirmed, but it is not a new loan. It was made one or two months ago when Finance Minister Song had not yet gone to the United States. There have been no new loans recently.

Japanese Navy Arrives in Shanghai

Part Headed to the Yangtze River

Part Stationed in Shanghai

The Japanese Naval Ministry, to strengthen its Yangtze River fleet, has selected a team of elite soldiers from the Sasebo naval unit. It has also selected an elite team of naval soldiers from six ships under the command of the Navy's First Fleet: the Mutsu, Yura, Haguro, Jinkei, Yubari, and Kinugasa, totaling 171 personnel. In addition, there are 12 technicians specializing in repairing military equipment: Shinohara, Kubo, Katayama, Mori Shinichi, Kota, Takeshita, Ogata Minoru, Takase. This group of soldiers is commanded by three officers dispatched by the Naval Ministry: Meguro Kousei, Reiko Motoichi, and Yoshioka Keisuke. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday from Kobe on the Japanese mail ship Nagasaki Maru. All officers and soldiers landed at the Wayside Wharf and proceeded to the headquarters of the Japanese Marine Corps in Hongkou. Part of the soldiers will be assigned to the 27th and 24th detachments on the Yangtze River, while others will be assigned to the Ataka and Fushimi ships and will depart for Hankou in the next few days. The majority of the soldiers will serve in the Shanghai Marine Corps. A batch of military equipment also arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru and has already been unloaded and stored in warehouses.

Ariyoshi Will Go North

The spokesman for the Japanese Consulate did not deny the news that Japanese Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi was about to travel north, but said that he was still waiting for instructions from the Japanese government, so it was not yet certain whether the trip would take place. As this concerns military diplomacy, I regret that I cannot comment.

Oppose Our Revised Tariffs

As for the Chinese government's revised tariff rates, which are much higher than before, especially affecting Japanese goods to a great extent, the Japanese government and merchants unanimously believe that this is an intentional attempt to boycott Japanese goods. Therefore, all parties are studying the details. If instructions from the Japanese government arrive in Shanghai, the Japanese Embassy will express its opposition to China.

It is reported that after Xiong and others arrived in Shanghai, they discussed the matter with members of the Shanghai Swastika Branch. Red Swastika Society Relief Team Treats Wounded and Nursing Women

I asked Wan Bi, Vice President of the Society, about everything. According to Wan, the relief work in North China was very detailed. The main points of his conversation are summarized as follows:

Since the outbreak of the Yuyu War, our Society has organized a relief team to implement relief efforts. After the war expanded, a total of 27 relief teams were organized and stationed in various key locations along the Great Wall and in the Luotang area to rescue wounded soldiers and refugees for three months without stopping for a single day. When leaving Beiping, Beiping and Tianjin were extremely tense. Red Swastika Society Relief Team Treats Wounded People

Regarding the placement of wounded soldiers, in addition to a portion being transported by the relevant divisions and brigades to safe locations, the remaining wounded soldiers admitted to the temporary hospitals of our Society in Beiping and Tianjin are now being transported separately to Shandong and Henan provinces through the Red Swastika Society for proper accommodation. Although the war has now stopped, conflicts still occur from time to time between the two sides, and casualties are still significant. The relief teams of our Society have been transferred from various passes of the Great Wall to appropriate locations to provide assistance at any time. At the same time, people from various places have fled to the Beiping and Tianjin areas due to changes in the war situation, and our General Society and local charitable organizations are separately accommodating them in designated places. There are many refugees, so the temporary accommodation centers established by our Society are already overcrowded. Even if peace is realized, the disaster areas will be vast and the houses will be in ruins. Hundreds of thousands of refugees will have nowhere to return, and various rehabilitation efforts will be difficult to resolve in the future. Other issues such as the placement of wounded soldiers after recovery and various temporary relief efforts in the Beiping and Tianjin areas are all urgent issues at present. President Xiong of our Society will return to Shanghai in a few days and will host people from all walks of life to report on the progress of relief efforts and discuss the above-mentioned issues, as well as discuss future continued relief efforts. I hope that all sectors will cooperate effectively so that there can be satisfactory results.

Lu Dipin, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, had previously gone to Beijing on official business. He has now completed his work and left Beijing the day before yesterday to return to Hangzhou. He had originally planned to return to the province on the Beijing-Hangzhou intermodal train, but he temporarily changed his plans and took the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River ship Jiang'an to Shanghai. When Lu boarded the ship, he changed his name and brought only four attendants. He lived alone in a large dining room and did not talk to anyone, so the passengers on the ship did not know that Chairman Lu was traveling with them. Lu was wearing a gray silk lined robe. It was not until yesterday morning, when the ship was about to arrive in Shanghai, that the military police escorting the ship learned of Chairman Lu's presence. The squad leader assigned two military policemen to stand guard outside Lu's room to show respect, but this caused Lu's displeasure. He ordered his attendants to inform the military police to remove the guard post to avoid attracting the attention of the passengers. At 10:30 AM, when the ship arrived at the Jinliyuan Wharf in Shanghai, Lu and his four attendants disembarked unobtrusively. A car that had been waiting for Lu at the wharf was already parked in advance. Chairman Lu boarded the car and went straight to his residence in Shanghai.

Shenxin No. 1 Factory Mediation Unsuccessful

Workers at the Shenxin No. 1 Cotton Mill in this port went on strike at 3:00 PM on the 25th and put forward conditions: (1) Restore the bonus system, (2) Fulfill the labor-capital contract, (3) Distribute past years' dividends, (4) Resolve pending cases, (5) Pay wages during the strike period. General Manager Rong Zongjing immediately went to the factory to persuade the workers, but failed to resolve the issue. At 9:00 AM on the 26th, Municipal Public Security Bureau Director Jiao Hongen, Wang Guangqing, Lu Yinshu, and representatives of various party and government agencies went to the factory to convene a meeting between labor and capital. The directors and chairmen believed that in the face of national crisis, unity should be the goal, and both labor and capital had their own difficulties and should understand each other. Subsequently, Rong Zongjing reported on the difficulties of the yarn industry and the factory. He had previously gone to Beijing to request assistance from the central government, but there were no effective solutions. He originally intended to implement a full suspension of night shifts, but for the sake of social stability and workers' livelihoods, he could only seek to reduce costs within the possible range to maintain operations as much as possible. However, the workers did not understand his difficulties and took advantage of the factory's difficulties, which was not in the workers' best interests. Subsequently, representatives of the labor union expressed their opinions, stating that the bonus system could not be completely abolished and that wages must be paid during the strike period. After Director Wen repeatedly advised them, both labor and capital felt his sincere mediation, and the meeting was about to conclude. It was already 6:00 PM. Director Wen and representatives of various party and government agencies were about to leave the factory, and the factory also sent personnel to start the motor. However, the workers suddenly rioted again, and the motor that had been started was shut down again, so there were no results.

Jisheng Society Receives Latest Shaanxi Disaster Report

The China Jisheng Society received a telegram yesterday from the Shaanxi Province Relief Affairs Association stating that the disaster in Shaanxi is severe and urgently requires relief. Heaven shows no mercy and has sent another strange disaster. According to reports from Pu, Lin, and Wei counties, on May 1st, black frost suddenly fell, followed by strong winds, and the remaining wheat seedlings withered completely. People are terrified, early autumn seeds are lacking, disaster victims are everywhere, and there is no way to seek help. They earnestly request assistance in raising funds for relief. Furthermore, a telegram from Qian Xiantian, the Magistrate of Mei County, stated, "Our country is poor, and Shaanxi is the poorest. Natural and man-made disasters have occurred for years, and Mei County is the most extreme. It is now the time between the green and yellow crops, and the people rely entirely on tree bark to survive. Although heaven has recently sent timely rain, but the amount obtained is small, and there is no hope for the summer and autumn harvests. There is a lack of seeds for autumn planting, the fields are barren, and artemisia is growing into forests. Without seeds at this time, how can we hope for a harvest? In the high autumn, the grass grows long, and the people of Mei County cannot avoid death. We have previously received relief and relied heavily on it for survival. The surviving people, who did not die in the famine year, will now die in a prosperous year. We are overwhelmed with anxiety and cannot rest. We earnestly request a large sum of money to save the disaster victims. Our descendants will be eternally grateful." Mr. Gu Jisheng, a standing committee member of the society, reported that he had personally investigated the situation and the tragic disaster was shocking. Those who have a heart to save the world, what should they think about this?

Foreign Fishing Vessels Coming to China

Anti-Dumping Duties Will Be Heavily Levied

In recent years, Japanese fishing boats have come to China to fish overseas, becoming more and more frequent. Recently, they have intensified their efforts. In addition to dumping the fish they catch in China, they are also transporting large quantities of fish from Japan to China for dumping. Taking Shanghai as an example, tens of thousands of dan of Japanese fish are transported each month, causing our country's fishing industry to be excluded and in imminent danger. As for the government's remedial measures, according to news from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, it will implement the collection of anti-dumping duties on foreign fishing vessels to resist. As for the collection method, no concrete decision has been made yet. Since last year, the customs has levied a regular tax of four yuan per dan on imported foreign fish. Unexpectedly, this year's fishing season is very prosperous, and Russian fish imports have also increased, so Japanese fish have greatly reduced prices for dumping, making it impossible for domestic fish to resist. If anti-dumping duties on foreign fish are not heavily levied, the future of domestic fish is unimaginable.
