Group Gymnastics Performance

At 10:20, the sports activities began. At the command of the starter, the track and field competition and the group gymnastics competition started simultaneously. Participants in the group gymnastics included Provincial High School, No. 11 Middle School, Municipal Middle School, Hangzhou Normal School, as well as private Qingbo, Shufan, Anding, Zongwen, Shiwu, Zhongshan, Zhengze, and Muxing Middle Schools. First, they gathered for morning exercises, with neat movements and energetic spirit. Then, the Provincial Girls' Middle School performed freehand exercises, and the Provincial High School performed flexibility exercises. The Zhijiang University Fitness Team temporarily joined to perform stacked pyramids, parallel bars, etc. Following that, Zongwen Middle School performed freehand flexibility exercises, Hangzhou Normal School performed dumbbell exercises, Shiwu Middle School performed flag exercises, Municipal Middle School performed freehand exercises, Provincial Hangzhou Normal School performed American-style flexibility exercises, Anding Middle School performed flexibility exercises, and Zhongshan Middle School performed Baduanjin exercises. The spirit of all participants was very good. Finally, over fifty members from the 236-member Philippine Chinese Overseas Children's Troupe, who had traveled to Hangzhou, joined to perform music, which was quite pleasant to listen to.

Competition Categories

This sports meet includes track and field, all-around, ball games, group gymnastics, health competitions, martial arts competitions, and shuttlecock competitions. There are many items, which are specifically classified as follows:

Men's Division

College/University Group: Limited to universities or specialized schools of equivalent level. A total of five schools participated. Track and field events are separated, but there are no school championships, only individual total scores are counted. This is similar to an open event.

Senior Group: Organized by district, with most athletes being middle school students. Track and field championships are awarded separately. Districts 1, 2, 3, and 4 all participated. This is the most important group in the Games.

Junior Group: Also organized by district, with track and field events combined into one championship. Everything else is the same as above.

Public Group: Organized by county, with a total of ten counties and one city (i.e., Hangzhou City) participating. Track and field championships are awarded separately.

Military/Police Group: Only four members from the Hangzhou City Guard Regiment participated. It does not really constitute a group, so there is no championship.

In addition, the all-around competition is organized by district, with four districts participating. There are also championships for swimming, soccer, basketball, tennis, baseball, and volleyball, all organized by district.

Women's Division

Track and field championships are divided into senior and junior levels. Participants are all organized by district. In addition, there are championships for swimming, basketball, tennis, volleyball, and softball.

Championship Classifications

In total, the men's division championships are divided into (1) Senior Track, (2) Senior Field, (3) Public Track, (4) Public Field, (5) Junior Track and Field, (6) All-Around, (7) Swimming, (8) Soccer, (9) Basketball, (10) Tennis, (11) Baseball, (12) Volleyball. Non-championship events include group gymnastics, health competitions, martial arts competitions, shuttlecock competitions, college/university group track and field, and military/police group track and field. The women's division championships are divided into (1) Senior Track and Field, (2) Junior Track and Field, (3) Swimming, (4) Ball (basketball), (5) Tennis, (6) Volleyball, (7) Softball. Non-championship events include group gymnastics, health competitions, martial arts competitions, and shuttlecock competitions.

Side Stories from the Games

Chen Bulei's Busy Reception: Chen Bulei, Vice President of the Games, has been promoting sports extensively since becoming the President of Zhejiang University. He arrived at the venue by car at 7:00 am, even before the staff, to personally supervise the workers in arranging refreshments at the podium and to welcome guests. He warmly greeted guests from various organizations and personally distributed a copy of the Games program to each person, attending to everyone and being exceptionally busy.

Instructors' Earnest Admonitions: To the left of the podium, several bamboo sheds were built for athletes to rest. Athletes sat on the ground, either rubbing their legs in preparation for the competition or chatting with each other. The team instructors gave instructions to the athletes, earnestly admonishing them about points of rule violation, hoping that they could create new records. The athletes listened attentively, with a calm attitude, seemingly confident of victory.

Athletes with Empty Stomachs: In the morning, there were only five sports events, but each event had five or six groups participating, held one after another, causing delays. The scheduled end time was 12:00, but the competition was still going on at 12:50. The athletes had arrived early in the morning, and by this point, they could not eat lunch, and were generally feeling the pangs of hunger.

Spectators Turned Drenched Chickens: Yesterday was Saturday, and most schools were closed. In the afternoon, students from various schools arrived in groups, and the number of spectators at the venue suddenly increased. Unexpectedly, the heavens were unkind, and a heavy rain suddenly poured down around 4:00 pm, turning the spectators into drenched chickens. Fortunately, the podium and the judgment, sports promotion departments still provided some shelter from the rain. The general female students, wearing thin clothes, had their figures revealed by the rain, and fled in disarray.

Referees Wading Through Mud and Water: Since the weather was uncooperative and the Games had many events to be completed within a limited number of days, it was not possible to stop. Chief Referee Jiang Xiangqing continued to give commands as usual. The referees could not quit and carried on with their work, wading through the mud and water. Under the heavy rain, the athletes were increasingly excited, which was admirable. Some quick-witted referees borrowed several umbrellas from the sports field to provide some shelter from the wind and rain, but the other referees suffered.

Mats Used as Umbrellas: The heavy rain lasted for an hour and still showed no sign of stopping. On the contrary, the wind and rain became more fierce. Due to the environmental constraints, the track and field events were forced to be suspended. The cloth sheds set up by the Boy Scouts at the venue lost their effectiveness. They hastily gathered their belongings, and each shed had a mat that was temporarily used as an umbrella. Four people shared one mat and sought shelter at the senior high school. All-Suzhou Women's Sports Meet

Held in a Heavy Downpour Zhenhua Girls' School Wins Group A Championship

Suzhou Women's Normal School Wins Group B Championship

Games Set Three New Records

(Suzhou, 27th) The third All-Suzhou Women's United Sports Meet was held yesterday (27th) afternoon in a heavy downpour. Thousands of spectators watched, and the athletes from various schools were also in high spirits, not showing any fear of the rain. Male and female guests alike stood upright in the heavy rain with umbrellas. The details of the various events are as follows:

Venue Order: The order at yesterday's venue was maintained by the Boy Scouts of Wuchu Elementary School, so it was quite orderly. At the entrance of Soochow University, twelve Boy Scouts from Suzhou Girls' Middle School were arranged on both sides.

Solemn Ceremony: At 2:00 pm, the opening ceremony was held. Athletes from various schools stood in three columns facing Lintang. Flags were raised, and the order was solemn. Ma ZhiKui from the County Sports Field gave a speech on behalf of the Director of Education.

Attending in the Rain: After the opening ceremony, the 50-meter and 100-meter finals began. The Soochow University sports field is 400 meters in circumference, so only the western end was used yesterday. Outside the ropes on the west side were all the Jinghai Girls, their school uniforms were pure white, resembling a short wall of powdered faces. Around 3:00 pm, due to the heavy rain, the guests all stood in a corner with umbrellas, looking out like a cluster of reeds and tents in a vast desert.

Quick Record of the Competition: After the start of the competition, the 50-meter final was held first. There were seven participants in Group A. Cheng Zhang Naiqi, lost by only one meter and came in second.

Later, in the Group A long jump, the first place was Chen Dingrui from Zhenhua, with a score of 3.94 meters. Normally, Chen's score would have been higher, but she suffered a minor foot injury during the preliminary round, which slightly reduced her performance.

Also, both Group A and Group B shot put events broke the previous record. In the Group A preliminary round, as many as 23 people participated. In the end, the first place was won by Huang Lianzhen, which was truly not easy.

The Group A 100-meter final was swept by Zhenhua School. It was unexpected that the school's talent was so evenly matched and rapidly improving.

Casual Talks

Talking About Wind and Moon

— Qi Fan

Let's not talk about state affairs, let's talk about wind and moon. However, looking at the forms of the two characters "wind" and "moon," even wind and moon are not necessarily easy to talk about.

Looking at the head of the character "wind," it seems to have the demeanor of a great power, and the head of the character "moon" also has a microcosm of a small court. The only difference is the openness and closure below. The character "state" guards the surrounding borders, forming a circle, while "wind and moon" do not care about these trivial matters. The top is heaven, the bottom is earth, north and south of the sky. The north is not guarded, and "wind and moon" symbolizes this. Could it be that the national crisis is caused by "wind and moon"?

Looking at the surface of the top, the character "wind" seems to have the demeanor of a great power, and a "worm" sits grandly in the middle. Even if this "worm" character has a stroke like a heavenly crown on top, a "worm" is still just a "worm." Isn't it very difficult to try to make it look good? As for the character "moon," within a small scope where the border is not guarded, there are two strokes that intersect, showing a tendency of two forces not yielding to each other. How can we hope for harmony and unity to face the outside world? It's strange that Cangjie created the characters in this way.

Now the two characters "wind and moon" are linked together. From the one with the demeanor of a great power to the microcosm of a small court, it is quite a sight of the Northern and Southern Song dynasties, which is a very ominous sign. Thinking this way, the two characters "wind and moon" really cannot be written down casually, let alone talked about. The so-called "talk" is never too much, a presentation of perspectives from all sides.

Looking at it this way, since state affairs are not easy to talk about, the truth is that "wind and moon" is also not easy to talk about. If you want to talk, you can only find topics other than "wind and moon" and state affairs, and the best model is "Today's weather, hahaha." Because if you say the weather is dull and bad, there is suspicion of slander, and if you say the sun is shining very well, you will be accused of supporting the Japanese flag and be labeled as a traitor to the country. Only a noncommittal hahaha about today's weather is the most clever way.

I have made a character-by-character examination of the two characters "wind and moon," clarifying that there is a truth that cannot be talked about. But we have mouths and must talk about something, and safety is what everyone hopes for. We cannot but carefully consider what to talk about to ensure safety and not betray the mouth we were born with. I hope that everyone within the seas will discuss this at length.

Shaw's Views on Reading Material

— Lin Yutang

(April 29th, British Pearsons Weekly published Shaw's remarks to students of the University of Hong Kong, revealing the secrets of reading and severely criticizing the learning of rote memorization, misleading younger generations. This confirms the words of Zheng Banqiao of the East, who said that scholars should "raise their spines." It shows that the views of heroes of ancient and modern times are similar and are definitely not just humorous deception. Young people who do not quickly "raise their spines," listen to rumors, parrot others, cheat for grades, cheat for diplomas, answer what the teacher wants you to answer, and take pride in getting A's and B's, should have the intelligence to realize that they have been fooled. If they don't even have this intelligence, they might as well get diplomas, write foreign-style stereotyped essays, hurry to get bachelor's, master's, and even doctoral degrees, to become useful talents to society, waiting to be slaughtered. The original article was in the form of a record and was not signed. It is now translated and introduced.)

I have a firm belief that all universities in the world should be torn down, leveled to the ground along with the walls and houses, and salt should be sprinkled on their foundations.

I often remind people that not long ago, culture was almost destroyed by the Great War. We don't yet know whether that war completely destroyed culture, but it doesn't matter much because this war has already proven one thing: that there wasn't much culture in the world to begin with.

That war was caused by people with university educations. There are actually the most dangerous classes in the world. One is the half-educated, who have destroyed half of the culture. Another is the fully educated, who have almost completely destroyed the world.

You should carefully read Professor Flinders Petrie's books.

When I was young丨 in those unbelievably ancient times 丨 no one knew what ancient civilizations were like. We only knew a little about Greece and Rome. Somehow, Rome collapsed, leaving behind a dark age. But before Professor Petrie excavated the ruins of ancient civilizations, no one knew how many civilizations like ours had existed before us. These civilizations were almost all destroyed by education. I think the reason for that is that to prevent civilizations from collapsing, we must have more original minds.

However, universities can only cultivate artificial minds. You come here, and they scoop out your brains and replace them with artificial minds. Therefore, I foresee that our culture will also completely collapse and return to the dark ages.

Of course, I don't know how you will choose. You may ask, "Should we leave the university?" or "Should we go out into the streets?"

I don't know. You can get some benefits from universities. You can get a kind of community life, which is very beneficial. If I had a son, I would advise him to go to school.

I would send him to university and say to him, "Be careful that they don't install an artificial mind in you. As for the books they want you to read, never read them."

A school textbook, by definition, is a book that cannot be read. The reason I was able to become an uneducated person is because I never read school textbooks.

When they required me to read textbooks, I was reading real books 丨 books by writers who could really write. Textbook authors will never belong to this category.

So I say, be careful to read real books, and textbooks should only be read enough to avoid being insulted and expelled.

Read good books, real books, and bury yourself in revolutionary books. Bury yourself in Marxism and all such theories. If you don't start a revolution at the age of twenty, then at fifty you can only become an old fossil. If you are a revolutionary of Marxism at the age of twenty, then at forty you may have some hope of not being outdated.

I can only say to all of you: Go in the direction I have indicated. Always argue with your teachers. If you have a history professor who has taught you his view of history, you should, if possible, say to him, "Hey, stop, we've heard your opinion, but you're about to find a professor who disagrees with you. Let's hear how you two debate."

All learning is repeated refutation. You will find that there is always a conspiracy to arbitrarily tell you to only see one side of things. Many young people enter university who are not qualified to be taught, but they must be given degrees. As a result, they can only be taught how to answer questions.

If you teach them both sides of a question, they will become confused. If you want to pass the exam, never seek the truth of right and wrong. You just have to go up and ask the teacher, "What answer do you want me to give to this question?"

Well, I'm very happy to have this opportunity to put poison in your brains. I hope you will laugh temporarily after listening, and you will all forget it in a week.

In my youth, I was a critic. I often wrote theater and art reviews for a weekly. Whenever I went to visit an art exhibition 丨 say, the Royal Academy 丨 I knew in my heart that I could only write one critical article. At most two articles, but there were two or three thousand pictures in the exhibition. My method was to quickly browse through them and pick out twelve or fifteen that were not "unbearably ugly" to criticize.

You should also take this approach. When your professors and mentors occasionally want to instill knowledge into you, you have to say, "I don't want anything that's not worth remembering."

You must be like garbage collectors, looking in the garbage heaps of history, seeing the value of the things you pick up, remembering the valuable ones, and discarding the rest.

In this way, you will become educated people; your minds will be filled with things worth remembering. Those who can remember everything that is not worth remembering often get the highest degrees. For these people, we only have one way to deal with them, which is to bury them.

Streets at Night

— Fang Zhizhong

The rain-washed street trees, their green coats studded with gold and jade beads, resemble a young woman after her bath, draped in light gauze, standing gracefully by the roadside. The electric lights, peeking through the dense shade of the street trees, watch the asphalt pavement, trod upon yet showing no trace of footsteps, and a pair of young men and women walking in sync. But the beggar huddled in the deep corner of the red wall will never be touched by the bright light waves.

"Master, grandma…have mercy…I haven't eaten for three days!" A sobbing cry emanated from the corner of the red wall.

On this quiet and noble road, in the residential area of ​​high-ranking Chinese and the upper classes of friendly nations, there is actually the moaning of a beggar—what a jarring sight! They glanced at it lightly, then turned their heads and continued their broad strides.

From the rows of automobile headlights and the shimmering streetlights, it was clear that she was of medium height, dressed in simple but neat student attire, her plump face radiating youthful heat; and he? Suited and booted, tall and thin. Her head leaned obliquely on his shoulder, his hand pressed tightly against her waist, they whispered, talked intimately, and walked side by side.

A burst of jazz music flew towards them, which was naturally more pleasant than the beggar's wail.

"Shall we go to the dance hall?" He kissed her hair.

She shook her head, saying nothing; he swallowed, unable to say anything. A moment of silence, broken only by the rhythmic crunching sound of their footsteps.

"Evening news! Want to see the Japanese bandits attacking Peiping and Tientsin! Want to see the Japanese bandits being defeated!…Four coppers a copy."

Although the news vendor's low voice broke the surrounding silence, it failed to attract their attention.

A cool breeze blew.

"I'm a little cold," she said.

He silently helped her with her coat, then returned to his original posture and moved towards the brightly lit XXX.

There were more broken-throated news vendors there, and more miserable wails from beggars, but these were fundamentally unstimulating! They continued to stroll under the graceful street trees, walking side by side, arm in arm, whispering intimately.

Carrot Top

— by Jules Renard, translated by Lin Qu

The Wind (Continued)

Lepic, as was his habit, walked from one window to the other. He repeatedly looked at the two children's report cards, paying particular attention to the notices written in person by the principal of the public middle school: the one about the eldest son, Felix, read:

"Impulsive by nature, but intelligent. Promising future."

The one about Carrot Top read:

"Achieves excellent results when he puts his mind to it, but does not often apply himself."

The thought that Carrot Top sometimes achieved excellent results amused the whole family. He now sat with his hands clasped on his knees, soaking his feet in water, feeling very glorious. He felt everyone scrutinizing him. In fact, people were learning to copy him by letting that head of long, dark red hair droop down, looking rather ugly. Lepic, unwilling to reveal his true feelings, only expressed his joy by joking around with him. When he walked past, he flicked his finger on his ear; when he walked back, he nudged him with his elbow. Carrot Top laughed happily.

Finally, Lepic put his hand in his messy hair, flicking his fingernails as if to crush some lice.

This was his playful way of showing affection.

But on the first flick, he crushed one.

"Ah, I got one!" he said. "I didn't miss!"

As he felt a slight disgust and rubbed his fingers on Carrot Top's hair, Lepic's wife raised her arms high:

"I suspected it all along," she said, looking very uncomfortable. "Good heavens! We're finally clean! Elise, quickly go and get a basin, you have something to do now."

The elder sister, Elise, brought a basin, a comb, and a pair of small saucers containing a little vinegar, and then began the hunt.

"Let me comb first!" the eldest brother, Felix, shouted. "I'm sure he gave them to me."

He scratched his head violently, wanting someone to give him a bucket of water to completely submerge his head in.

"Don't make a fuss, Felix," said the elder sister, Elise, who liked to help others. "I won't hurt you." She put a cloth around his neck, with the care and patience that a mother has for her son. She separated his hair with one hand and gently held the comb with the other. She neither looked disgusted nor afraid of getting them on herself. She searched for lice for him.

Whenever she said, "Another one!" the eldest brother, Felix, kicked the bottom of the bucket and threatened Carrot Top with his fists, who waited silently for his turn.

"You're done, Felix," said the elder sister, Elise. "You only had seven or eight; you can go and count. Now let's see how many Carrot Top has."

With the first comb, Carrot Top got more than that. The elder sister, Elise, thought she had found a nest of lice, but she had only accidentally caught a group.

Everyone stood beside Carrot Top. The elder sister, Elise, combed intently. Lepic stood with his hands behind his back, watching Elise work like a curious stranger. Lepic's wife complained from time to time.

"Ah! Ah!" she said, "We need a shovel and a rake for this."

The eldest brother, Felix, squatted on the ground shaking the basin to collect the lice that fell from the comb. These lice fell with bits of scalp. We could see their tiny legs, like eyelashes, moving. They were shaken around in the basin and soon killed by the vinegar.

US Abandonment of Gold Standard Causes

Sharp Fall in Gold Price of $18.70

丨Guangdong Banks Unleash Over Two Thousand Bars丨

The gold market experienced a significant drop yesterday. Although the overseas silver market initially showed a downward trend in the morning, the rise in US cotton and stocks was quite strong. The market opened at $965, down $9.50 from the previous closing. News of the US President Roosevelt's decision to formally abandon the gold standard, sent via Reuters, triggered a wave of selling. Fook Cheong, Bing Hing, and others aggressively sold, driving the opening price lower. Further anticipation that the measure would pass, coupled with news of rising gold mine stocks and the ability of debtor nations to repay war debts in any US currency, fueled a market-wide sell-off. Large players unloaded bars, particularly Guangdong's Hang Hing, which aggressively released over a thousand bars. The exchange rate hardened as a result. However, late buying interest from banks and arbitrage activities among dealers, particularly Dalian banks, led to a recovery. Spot added $60, May-June swaps were priced at a discount of $22.50, and May-July at $34. The pricing issue has been revised by the council, aiming to maintain the $24 calculation, but with adjustments based on changes in gold weight, using the initial HSBC exchange rate for British and American currencies as a standard, calculated monthly. The US exchange rate will still be settled at $24. This proposal is awaiting discussion by the brokers' association today (Sunday). The market conditions for the half-day are recorded below:

The market opened at $965, down $9.50 from the previous closing. Physicals opened at $5.50. Spring and Autumn

Injustice for Men

— Zhanlu

In this era of women's empowerment, men naturally have many grievances. However, my piece "Injustice for Men" is not a reflection arising from women's empowerment. Even if women are not empowered, men still bear two kinds of "wrongful burdens of sin." What two kinds? Listen to me explain:

(1) The ideographic meaning of the characters for man and woman is that "strength in the fields" is man, and "broom" is woman. This shows that shouldering a plough is a man's duty, and holding a broom is a woman's natural role. According to the rules, street sweeping duties on the road and cleaning work in the city should be performed by women. However, that is not the case. There are only street sweepers, not street sweeper women; there are only sanitation workers, not sanitation worker women. What is the reason that the broom next to the woman character is transferred to the hands of men? Alas! Wrongful burden of sin!

(2) Because the Han Dynasty was a strong era in China, Chinese people are called Han people. By extension, men are Han men, and good men are good Han men. What an honor! Ever since the term "Han traitor" came into being, women have been saying it loudly. "Han traitors, Han traitors, are all men. Therefore, those who are lackeys of the Japanese are all cursed as Han traitors, and no one curses them as traitor women. This shows that being a Han traitor is a male profession." However, that is not the case. Among the spies, there are many female spies. Once they are exposed, everyone also curses them as Han traitors, and does not specially give them the title of traitor woman. It is the fate of men to be unlucky. Alas! Wrongful burden of sin!

Don't Talk About State Affairs

— Hualing

In any casual teahouse, there is always a sign hanging that says, "Beware of Pickpockets." Some more cautious tea servers simply add a red paper strip next to "Beware of Pickpockets," writing "Don't Talk About State Affairs." In fact, what's the big deal about talking about state affairs? You just shouldn't talk乱, that's all. For example, "Our army's broadsword team killed the enemy soldiers so that they were holding their heads and shouting daddy repeatedly." Then, just say how the enemy soldiers are脓包and you definitely won't be regarded as a "Han traitor," "enemy spy," or "troublemaker." If it's "Our army retreats at lightning speed," or "Due to strategic reasons, we are changing to a new defensive line," and your esteemed self is "talking about state affairs" in a place that happens to be just outside of "that new Chen line that is calmly responding to the battle," then a mouthful of "benevolent rule" and "paradise" would be to describe the enemy soldiers' gang rape of some old woman. At least you should say, "How fortunate the old woman is." I can vouch for this, patting my chest, that you can talk about state affairs all your life and you won't get your head chopped off.

"Don't Talk About State Affairs." The "three old men at the bridgehead" in teahouses might still respectfully obey the tea server's orders. But if news reporters who rely on "talking about state affairs" to earn a living also regard "Don't Talk About State Affairs" as the golden rule, wouldn't that be terribly, terribly bad?

Actually, that's not the case. News reporters have their own methods for "talking about state affairs." For example, if the person in power says, "The suffering Chinese people," the news reporter will expound on the two words "suffering" to the fullest extent. Furthermore, if the elders say, "What crime have the young men committed? The crime lies with the old men," then the news reporter will write straight in his pen, "What crime have the highly respected elders committed? The crime lies with the old people who don't care about state affairs." If news reporters "talk about state affairs" and "lead public opinion" in this way, they will definitely not resist the wet wood tip, and perhaps they can leap to a position. Therefore, those who恪遵 to "Don't Talk About State Affairs" are the greatest fools in the world. Those who "talk about state affairs" without looking at the wind direction are also great fools.

Hong Foshi's Novels

— Jielu

Speaking of this matter, it has been more than twenty years ago. In revolutionary history, perhaps it has some value for records. During the last years of the Qing Dynasty, when the relatives of the imperial family were in power and the country was in decline, the court used the talk of "preparing for constitutionalism" to deceive the people. Several enlightened patriots borrowed the running of newspapers as the mouthpiece for promoting revolution. Although the literary net was still tight at that time, they had to hide their swords in scabbards and write with veiled language, but there was something in their words. However, a burst of "vitality" seemed even stronger than today's newspapers. Yu Sao-xin (Youren) ran a newspaper called "Min Hu Bao" (People's Appeal), but it was soon banned by the Qing government. Mr. Yu dug out the two eyes of the character "Hu" (Appeal), and "Min Yu Bao" (People's Exhortation) appeared. Coincidentally, at this time, Zhejiang was experiencing the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Incident, and the general manager Tang Zhexian (Shouqian) started the Tianduo Bao. He hired Cixi Chen Tianying (Xunzheng) as general manager, Hong Foshi (Yunxiang) as editor-in-chief, Feng Shigong (Kai) as the novelist, and Hu Piaowa (Liangzhen) as the editor. Except for Mr. Tang, it was completely a Cixi people's Qing dynasty. After Tianduo was published, it suddenly released a different color in the newspaper industry, with Haohaodangdang's Foshi editorials, very much in the style of the owner of the Bingyin Room. There were also the Qingli and elegant Shigong notes and novels, enough to compete with the Pingdeng Pavilion notes of that time, and the cold-blooded and amused novels, and everyone came out to show off.

However, at this time, Shenxin and the two newspapers took the business community as their position and did not carry any color. The Times seemed to be close to the Liang Rengong faction. (The current Times is no longer run by Di Pingzi, and its nature has completely changed.) Min Yu had some fire, and Tianduo had a special flavor, containing the revolutionary anti-Manchu goods, which was the same. Later, Tianduo also hired Dai Tianchou (Chuanxian), who is now the president of the Examination Yuan; and Chen Bulei (Xunen), who is now the director of the Zhejiang Education Department. Both of them were young and handsome, and their papers were indulgent and rebellious, awakening a lot of the decadent people's spirit at that time. Later, Li Huaishuang (Jiarong) came to take over the post of editor-in-chief, Liu Yazi (Qiji) came to be the editor, and Zou Yayun (Quan) compiled the essays, all of whom were Nanshe veterans. The revolution had already succeeded, and the Tianduo Bao was in its golden age.

Now I will talk about Mr. Hong. Mr. Hong, from Shanbei, Cixi, personal name Yunxiang, style name Qiaoling, "Foshi," "Canfo," and "Tianzui" were all pen names in Tianduo Bao. Mr. Youxue was studying in Japan in his early years; he liked wine, was good at poetry and writing, and had served as a professor of history and geography in various universities in the North and South. I have always called him "Ningbo Wu Zhihui," but Wu was滑稽, while Hong was耿直, and their knowledge was very similar. Mr. Hong has a deep knowledge of Buddhism, and is friendly with Xie Wuliang (Meng) in Sichuan. Mr. Xie wrote a eulogy when Mr. Xie passed away last month: "He traveled with the bell and drum, and the drunkard was generous and patriotic: He sang proudly from the phoenix tree, and the poetry scrolls were still full of his home." To call Mr. Hong a "drunkard" and "poet," Mr. Hong would definitely agree if he knew in the afterlife. Mr. Hong wrote "The Daughter of Liu Hui," which is a Taoist novel. "Sister of the莽 Monk," is a Buddhist novel. Both works are written in the style of the Tang Dynasty, and have the same wonderful effect as the novels of Monk Manshu. It is amazing and brilliant, and it is really beyond the reach of mediocre people. It is not impossible to call Mr. Hong a "novelist."

Amateur Weekly

From the Economic Collapse to Urban Dilemmas

The introduction of capitalism into Chinese villages has, on one hand, increasingly tied Chinese agricultural production to the commodity system. The daily necessities required by rural China are ever more dependent on urban markets that supply goods. On the other hand, it has destroyed the home handicrafts that served as a sideline in rural areas, making them gradually need independent production departments that are different from agricultural taxes. The former increases the expenses of the peasants, while the latter reduces their income, thus making the peasants vulnerable to hunger and threats. The excessive levies of taxes, the heavy burden of land rent, and the piercing exploitation of commercial and usurious capital—all these are the feudal forces' seizure of the peasant masses, intensifying the process of peasant impoverishment. At the same time, there are often civil wars among Chinese warlords, with the conflicts among the various imperialists as their backdrop, which further burden the peasants with pre-war provisions, wartime requisitions, harassment, destruction (the so-called disasters of war), and various post-war reconstruction expenses. The Chinese peasant masses, caught in such a process of impoverishment, have no choice but to gradually reduce the scope of their production, and agricultural techniques can only become increasingly crude, with no possibility of improvement. As for the improvement of water conservancy, it is naturally out of the question. These are all important phenomena reflected in the essential nature of the collapse of China's rural economy. In other words, China's rural economy has collapsed under the dual exploitation of imperialist economic aggression and feudal forces.

The natural and man-made disasters that have occurred in various Chinese cities over the years, whether interchangeably or continuously, are merely the general manifestations of the collapse of China's rural economy, especially the great flood of the year before last and the disastrous bumper harvest of last year, which further demonstrated the universality and depth of this pattern.

The result of the collapse of China's rural economy, in addition to causing death, displacement, banditry, and unrest, has also led to a further decline in the purchasing power of the peasants and a further shrinking of the Chinese market. This has at least two kinds of impact on industry. One is that the sales of industrial manufactured goods are further reduced; urban industry not only loses its basis for expansion, but is also bound to shrink. The second is that a large number of unemployed peasants constitute a crowded situation in the urban and rural labor market, leading to a general reduction in wages, a general impoverishment of workers' lives, a decline in workers' purchasing power, and the market shrinks once again, forcing industry to contract even further.

Looking at the various sectors of Chinese industry, whether traditional specialized industries or modern mechanized industries, they have all become extremely desolate recently. For example, the famous Hangzhou silk industry is in such a state of decline that it is unimaginable, leading to a trend of work stoppages. The old-style silk weaving industry is like this, and the new-style textile industry is no better. The recent reduction of work at Shanghai yarn factories is said to be influenced by the dumping of Japanese goods, but the shrinking of sales over the years cannot be said to be unrelated, can it?

So, what will happen to urban commerce? Can it avoid this crisis and prosper independently? Here, let us use only the most obvious fact of sales as a basis for explanation.

In recent years, especially recently, because the reduced market cannot accommodate the already reduced production volume, a strange phenomenon of massive price reductions has been created. This phenomenon is now widespread throughout China. In any place, in front of the shops, there are usually constantly changing tactics, either saying "big price reduction," or "giving away gifts," or "discounting"... Occasionally walking down the street, one can receive several advertising leaflets for silk and satin, pharmacies, tea shops, and shoe stores, as if the customers have not visited their doors for a hundred years, creating a phenomenon that has never existed before. As for scheduled price reductions, there must be grand celebrations for several weeks of anniversaries and the usual seasonal events for spring, summer, autumn, and winter; and after the expiration date, they thank their customers for their patronage and extend the period again, continuously without end. Shanghai, known for its prosperity, is considered the most concentrated place for consumers, and this phenomenon of price reductions is also occurring continuously. The large price reduction flags fluttering in the wind in front of major companies and stores on various roads, or the broadcasts from gramophones and radios, are competing to do their best to attract customers, and even during the cheap period, there are so-called specially cheap goods, and so on. All this, on the surface, seems like a lively event, but in essence, is it not a sign of the depression of urban commerce!

Life: I Sold My Eyes

— Zhen Xin

(Proofread) The reasons why I abandoned my position as an elementary school teacher and became a proofreader in a bookstore are roughly the following two, but now I realize that these are two reasons that are completely unfounded.

First, the work is easy. Everyone who has not been a proofreader thinks that proofreading is the easiest job in the literary field. As long as one can read books and has a little knowledge of various sciences, it is more than enough to be a proofreader; I thought so at first too. But in reality, it is not the case at all. Is it possible to ensure that there is not a single mistake in a thick book of one hundred thousand or two hundred thousand words? With sloppy and confused manuscripts, with the styles of various schools and genres, describing all kinds of specialized knowledge, as well as blurred proofs and glossy paper that reflects white light, is it possible to ensure that there are no mistakes under these conditions? Moreover, one must also pay attention to the most easily overlooked page numbers, headings, and spines, and perhaps the printing workers secretly give you some hard-to-detect flaws. Under these conditions, is it possible to ensure that there are no mistakes? Now I am convinced that being a proofreader is more difficult than being an editor.

Second, one can gain more knowledge. Everyone has this idea, thinking that by doing proofreading, one can read many books for free and improve one's knowledge. Didn't I think so at first? But now I know that this is like buying a champagne ticket and wanting to win four hundred and twenty thousand or five hundred thousand—a complete fantasy. If a proofreader only focuses on the meaning of the book and does not pay attention to each individual word that makes up that meaning, then I believe that after publication, there will be many mistakes and he will be met with cold stares from the bookstore owner or the newspaper editor. The editor-in-chief's job is to determine acceptance or rejection from the viewpoint of the entire book and the subject matter (accept or return); the editor's job is to determine acceptance or rejection in each paragraph and each sentence (modify); and the proofreader's job is to determine acceptance or rejection in each individual word. Because the duties are different, the focus of attention is also different. The proofreader only pays attention to each word, such as the difference between "裏" and "裹," the difference between "已" and "巳," the difference between "綱" and "網," and the difference between "逈" and "迴," and so on. Can attention to each of these words increase knowledge? It is just like the joke of the blind men touching the elephant.

So, what do I actually get from this job? Yes, that is "I sold my eyes," and the price is only a monthly salary of ten-odd yuan!

I have been a proofreader for less than a year, and I have already changed to a pair of nearsighted glasses that are one hundred degrees deeper than before. Now I can no longer see clearly the gold characters of XX Lane, XX Fang. This is not only true for me alone; none of my colleagues are not obviously aware of it. Because of this, we have also thought of many remedies, such as using green gauze covers on electric lights, asking the printing house to print the reverse side of the proof (i.e., the rough side of the glossy paper), and so on. But even so, selling our eyes is still the same, only the difference between fifty steps and a hundred steps.

Lao Zhang stood idly, while Lao Wang stood in the shade, watching angrily.

The sun was baking him like fire. He was a pale, haggard, and weak child. He used his weak hands to push the lead bucket forward. Lime leaked from the small holes, leaving white straight lines on the ground, forming a rectangle.

The lines were drawn. Lao Wang and Lao Zhang stood facing each other, each holding a tennis racket. They began to hit the ball, hitting it quickly to see who was better. The ball jumped back and forth over the net, and the rackets hit it, making a crisp sound.

He stood straight beside them, like a piece of wood. Suddenly, when he was not prepared, a ball hit him on the head. The ball was heavy, and it raised a bump on his forehead, causing a burning pain. He did not shout because shouting was useless.

"Can't you be more careful?" Lao Wang said to him, "Stupid thing!"

Lao Zhang shrugged his shoulders and smiled.

They continued to hit the ball. As if attacking an enemy, they gritted their teeth, used all their strength, and hit wildly. The ball flew out like a bullet.

So he—that child—quickly started running, his legs and arms like wings. After running dozens of steps, he grabbed the solid ball and threw it back with all his might. He had already used all his strength, but the ball still could not reach the court.

"Have you eaten? So weak!"

Sometimes, they hit lightly, and the ball did not go over the net, but fell in front of them. To avoid getting hit on the head by the ball, this child dared not step into the court. So they got angry again: "If you don't come to pick up the ball, what are you waiting for!"

The ball was always so unpredictable, sometimes going east and sometimes west. He kept running after it, as if a shuttlecock string was pulling him on the ball. He ran until he was drenched in sweat, but he still kept running.

The sun was high in the sky. Lao Wang and Lao Zhang had already drunk five bottles of soda.

Gasping for breath, he felt his legs heavy in the hot sunlight, as if they were tied with two lead cakes. He stood there blankly, his whole body so weak that he almost collapsed.

But Lao Wang and Lao Zhang were both smiling. They continued to hit their ball as if nothing had happened, still shouting in that rude tone: "Kid, go pick up the ball quickly!"

Current Affairs Research

A General Review of the Yarn Factory Layoff Problem

— Zhang Yunshi

At present, in China's serious political and economic problems, in addition to the crazy invasion of Japanese imperialism, the most obvious evidence of the thorough bankruptcy of national industry is the recent implementation of work reduction in yarn factories across the country. The invasion of Japanese imperialism is enough to subvert the entire nation's life, and the yarn factory layoffs are the most obvious proof of the thorough bankruptcy of national industry.

In the storm of layoffs implemented by yarn factories across the country, we can hear three different voices. One is standing on the position of the capitalists, saying that the factory's layoffs are a last resort. In the current situation of overproduction of cotton yarn, if the factory does not reduce work in time, it will be completely bankrupt. At that time, the workers will not even be able to find half a job, which is what is called "If the skin does not exist, what will the fur adhere to?" Therefore, the current implementation of layoffs by yarn factory capitalists is indeed for their own benefit on the one hand, but it is also thinking for the workers on the other hand. One is standing on the interests of the workers, saying that in this time of national economic bankruptcy and numerous unemployment, the workers' original wages are already insufficient to live on, and now they have to reduce work (actually reducing wages), which is tantamount to putting the workers to death. Therefore, yarn factory capitalists should not only care about their own interests and implement layoffs. Another is the third party's statement between the two, in the third party's opinion, the yarn factory capitalists' layoffs are out of necessity, and the workers' opposition also has half the truth. However, the best way is in this autumn of national crisis, the workers must always appreciate the capitalists' difficulties, suffer temporarily, and work hard to produce in order to save China. In the future, when the national disaster turns into national celebration, the foundation of yarn factories across the country will be consolidated, and the lives of the workers can be improved. In fact, in my opinion, except for the worker's side being precious, the rest are nothing but "scratching the surface." Whether in theory or practice, there are shortcomings.

We know that Chinese workers, especially yarn factory workers, are the most miserable. The working hours are particularly long, but the wages are particularly meager, so meager that they simply cannot maintain their lives. This is a well-known fact. Now, because of the overproduction of cotton yarn and the shrinking of the market, the resulting result is of course to starve all the yarn factory workers in China to death one by one. On this point alone, yarn factory capitalists and the government have no way to defend themselves. Therefore, in any case, yarn factory capitalists should never disregard the lives of workers because of temporary difficulties.

Conversely, the immature Chinese industry is indeed at the end of its rope at the moment and urgently needs to be saved. However, before taking measures to save it, one must understand its root causes in order to prescribe the right medicine and have an effect. Otherwise, giving up eating because of choking is not the right way, and it may even aggravate the severity of all domestic panic and chaos. Yarn factory layoffs are such a phenomenon.

The reason why Chinese industry cannot develop and is instead declining day by day is solely because it has been invaded by imperialists. The inability to control tariffs and the inability to recover concessions have led to diseases such as the dumping of foreign goods and the monopoly of foreign capital. Since the "September 18th" and "January 28th" incidents, the four northeastern provinces have fallen into the hands of the Japanese, and the Songhu area has been completely destroyed by the Japanese army's artillery fire. Then came market shrinkage, political chaos, economic bankruptcy, increased unemployment... etc., which are fatal blows, and the overproduction of Chinese cotton yarn is naturally inevitable. Therefore, to save the major crisis of yarn factories across the country, it is not to reduce work, but to actively resist the invasion of Japanese imperialism and the oppression of other imperialists. If it is not like that, even if the workers' work and wages are reduced to the point where they cannot be reduced, they cannot save this dying fate. Why is it that Chinese capitalists do not dare to raise the banner of anti-imperialism? They will only meekly submit to them, allowing them to oppress and exploit, while turning around and desperately trying to get back the losses they have suffered from the Chinese workers. The implementation of layoffs in yarn factories across the country is the most obvious example.

Therefore, if we stand on the position of the interests of the entire nation, we should unconditionally oppose the yarn factory layoffs. Because this kind of layoffs cannot save the crisis of yarn factories across the country and is enough to put countless workers to death. To solve the crisis of yarn factories, there is only liberation of China, and conversely, only when China is liberated can China's cotton textile industry and other industries be prevented from declaring bankruptcy.

People's Little Parliament

On "Promoting Domestic Goods" and "Labor-Capital Coordination"

— Discussion by Councilor He Xingxiu

(Fourth Discussion on the Case of How to Maintain the Livelihood of Laid-Off Yarn Factory Workers)

In the last issue of this magazine, Yiping-jun spoke voluminously about this issue, but at the root of it all, it was nothing more than "promoting domestic goods" and "labor-capital cooperation."

It is said that China has boycotted Japanese goods twelve times. Of course, the "promotion of domestic goods" that followed has also happened twelve times. However, as a result, Japanese goods have been boycotted once, and sales have become more prosperous once. Domestic goods, despite being promoted, cannot be promoted. This is not as simple as what some people say is a "five-minute fever," nor is it as simple as Yiping-jun said is "the dumping of foreign goods." The question is why foreign goods are dumped and why domestic goods cannot be promoted.

Capitalism, when it stormed into the old and large China, had already reached its final stage and regarded the discovery of such a large market as a life-saving elixir. All capitalist countries want to monopolize it, but because of mutual containment, they maintain the independence of a "Republic of China." Such independence is already an extraordinary favor, and are they willing to let Chinese national capital rise up to oppose them? Therefore, they used methods such as "tariff agreements" and "establishing factories in China"... many methods to oppress China's emerging industries. At the same time, national capitalists, for their own survival, had to surrender and become compradors. National capital has no possibility of construction at all. Isn't "promoting domestic goods" a big joke?

As for the high-sounding tunes of "labor-capital cooperation" and "labor-capital coordination," they have been sung for many years, but what is the result? These two antagonistic forces, which have no room for compromise, have launched a bloody struggle. The so-called "being in the same boat," etc., seem to have become good-sounding terms in the mouths of the rich. Because Yiping-jun's consciousness is incorrect, the conclusion he draws, such as "industry and commerce are unusually developed, the national life is very active, and the lives of workers will naturally improve," will become a golden check that can never be cashed!

So, what is the way out for the workers? In my personal opinion, workers only have a way out under the premise of uncompromising resistance.

Sanatorium for the Mentally Ill

Yearning

— Yang Fuwan

At present, the misery of the masses' lives is an undeniable fact. We shop assistants can continue to maintain our jobs in the current society where there are hundreds of millions of unemployed people, which seems to be "uniquely blessed." However, the happiness of a few contrasts with the difficulty of our lives. The oppression and exploitation of the imperialists have aroused our weak sense of sorrow. Material enjoyment, the prosperity of the streets... are all enough to stir up our desires. We cannot idealistically say that we want to suppress our desires, and at the same time, we cannot use the philosophy of "settling down and establishing a life" and "not competing with the world" to comfort our souls. So some of us spend our days pursuing some elusive and vague yearnings, and some wait quietly for these yearnings to come. But what exactly are these yearnings? What are we pursuing and expecting?

First, are we expecting "upward mobility"? "Upward mobility" means that a young man will become a big boss, a female worker will become a shop owner (recently, there was a domestic film with such a plot, but it is still a movie), and a young apprentice will climb to the position of factory owner. Haven't the wondrous stories of past tycoons inspired us? Wasn't Xi Guansheng a big boss from a young apprentice? Wasn't Edison a big capitalist from a young newspaper vendor? And weren't many wealthy people like Hartung and Da Lai "of humble origins"? So there are some people who can write well who say: "As long as you can be sincere and earnest, thrifty and hardworking, there will be a day when you can climb to the top!"—especially in amateur weekly magazines, you can often see such articles. Yes, these miracles are all true, but it is a pity that they have lost their "time." In the early days of capitalism, these miracles would happen and should happen, but now, capitalism is old and powerful. It has exerted its authority, and no one in its domain is allowed to climb in from the bottom. So "time" tells us that such expectation has become a boundless dream!

Second, let's step back and not expect "upward mobility," but expect "mediocrity." Let's not want to become a rich man, but just want to become a "comfortable middle-class family." But capitalism's inherent illness has reached the point of no cure. Roosevelt, MacDonald... and what Heleyo, Hitler... and the like, are desperately trying to find a panacea, but it is useless. What London Conference cannot cure this terminal illness. Overproduction, low purchasing power, and the decline of industry and commerce. As the days go by, the vast unemployed population created by capitalism is becoming more and more vast. This "recession" tide has already engulfed the entire world, and future unemployment will soon fall on our heads. Even if we want to be law-abiding citizens "living and working in peace" under capitalism, I am afraid that it is almost impossible. In this way, our second yearning has become a moon in the water!

So, we can't think, if we think, we will smile bitterly!

Finally, let me borrow the words of a friend—he is a shop assistant in a large store on Nanjing Road—to conclude this article. He said: "In the past, during our store's big sales, we would sell more than 10,000 yuan a day. Now, it's good if we can sell 1,000 yuan. And our store's expenses are more than 700 yuan a day. Can we continue to maintain this? At this time, the boss will of course have something to say: reduce expenses, lay off staff, then we will have to roll away. I am hopeless, but what about the rest of the majority?

Aren't the yarn factory layoffs also leaving the workers with no way out? Looking at the world situation, isn't the future world war about to break out? After the outbreak, China will of course become a slaughterhouse, and we in this group are afraid that we will become wronged souls under the guns. We have nothing to look forward to. We are only waiting for unemployment and death!"

But are we really waiting for "unemployment and death"? Can't we use our own strength to accelerate the removal of the root causes that cause our unemployment, poverty, and death? Maybe that's a "way out"!

Little Amateur Police Life Special Issue

Suppressing Bandits

— Ke Zixiang

Public Security Head Officer County Police

The life of a police officer is as monotonous and dull as a dry well, especially in a lonely small county town like ours. But recently, there have been rumors that bandits have appeared in Yangjiawa near the county town, and the county magistrate has issued an official order to the Public Security Bureau, requiring us to cooperate with the Public Security Brigade to eliminate them as soon as possible. So I, along with other dispatched colleagues and the Public Security Brigade, went to the bandits' lair with great effort.

Our leader was the captain of the Public Security Brigade. He was a true northerner, a large man who only knew how to boast. He always started his sentences with: "Damn your mother, no guts."

This time we saw that he had guts. He walked ahead with great fanfare. After less than five li, we sat down to rest because we needed to conserve our energy to fight. The brigade captain, full of energy, lectured us, sincerely teaching us many impractical tactics for suppressing bandits. For example, "When a machine gun comes, lie down and roll forward. Don't be afraid of hand grenades..." We were all tired of hearing these words. Finally, he suddenly said to us excitedly: "Brothers, this time you must do your best for the local people and give these dog bandits a good beating." Sure enough, we were all excited, and our legs were eager to get up immediately. After about a quarter of an hour, we set off again.

We all knew that the bandits were in Yangjiawa, but we didn't know where in Yangjiawa. After all, the brigade captain was resourceful. He stopped in front of a teahouse and shouted inside aimlessly: "We are here to fight bandits in Yangjiawa. Does anyone know where the bandit den is?" Immediately, a man in his thirties stood up and said he knew. We asked him to lead the way, and he agreed, walking proudly side by side with the captain.

The team advanced along a series of earthen hills. The early autumn sun was as hot as the dog days of summer. We walked, complaining and covered in sweat. Everyone forgot the purpose of moving forward, walking as if lost in a dream.

When we were in a semi-dormant state, suddenly a loud noise erupted from the woods on the left, like a giant hammer striking a wooden barrel. It was undoubtedly a gunshot. Like wild rabbits, we scurried in all directions. As for the brigade captain, he was already lying on the ground like a dead cow, scolding us with his face sideways: "Damn your mother, lie down!" We inexplicably gathered together and lay down. Strangely, the villager who led the way stood there without any surprise, still with a foolish smile. Although the brigade captain lying next to him tried his best to punch his leg, telling him to lie down, he stubbornly stood there. A few minutes passed, and the surroundings were still silent. The villager became impatient and urged us to hurry. The bolder ones stood up first and looked around, but no bullets were flying, so they disappointedly called everyone. So everyone stood up and asked each other about the source of the gunshot. The villager suddenly said plainly: "This was a shooter (meaning a hunter) firing."

We walked silently for a few more li, and the guide said that the old nest was almost here. We could see it by turning around this woods. Turning around the woods, there were indeed five or six thatched huts at the foot of the earthen hill. Who would have thought that these very ordinary small houses would be ambushed by a group of strong men? So the team stopped unanimously. The brigade captain told the villager to go and see how many bandits were inside and what they were doing. But the villager refused to go. He said: "Sir, they have weapons." The captain turned around and asked us: "Which of you brothers will go and take a look?" But no one answered. "Damn your mother, no guts," the captain said again. "Fire! Shoot over there!" Everyone lay on the ground and fired at the few silent thatched houses. After less than thirty or forty shots, seven or eight men and women ran out, fleeing along the foot of the hill in panic. No bullets flew towards us. One of the fugitives fell, and another tried to help him in a panic. We surrounded them and captured both of them.

We were victorious. As expected. We went to a nearby village for a meal. After the meal, I chatted with an old woman. I said: "We have captured the bandits for you. No one will bother you anymore." But she said unhappily: "Bandits, bandits only eat our chickens. The lords in your city will even eat our chicken droppings. They don't have the ability to catch bandits, but they tie up good people." But I still didn't believe her. We worked so hard, were so frightened, and fired so many shots. Could we be wrong? And we came to fight bandits, isn't this person the one we wounded?

A Chilled Heart

— Wang Zexiang

From Soldier to Police

Our police station's lunch time is at 10:00 AM. The station provides the rice, but we have to buy our own dishes. We always eat: tofu, pickled vegetables, dried tofu, canned fish, over and over again. Even if it were better, where would we get the money?

One day after lunch, I chatted with a brother, a Shandong man. I learned that he was a soldier before, and participated in the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army. He was hit by a Japanese dwarf in the head while fighting in Jinan. Later, for some reason, the officers told them: "Now the revolution is successful, you can leave!" They gave each person a few silver dollars and disbanded. He wandered here and became a policeman. At first, he hoped to be promoted slowly, but after a few years, he remained the same. He often dreamed of going back to his hometown, but with a monthly salary of eleven dollars, four dollars were deducted for food, and he had to buy his own dishes, bathe, get a haircut, wash his clothes... and he hadn't been paid for two months. Fate nailed him firmly to "misfortune" like an iron nail, and the future of his life was hopeless!

He talked to me about the scenery of his hometown, about his family who were still eking out a living under the grace of the landlord. He fell silent. I knew that in a corner of the distant sky, in a corner of his soul, there was a gray-haired mother, a emaciated child, and: how lovely the bright mountains and forests were! The longing for his homeland broke his heart, and sorrow occupied his heart.

As for myself, I shared the same fate as him. Every time I thought about the monthly salary of eleven yuan, deducting four yuan for food, dish money, haircuts, bathing, washing clothes... my heart also chilled.

Specializing in Self-Employment Introduction

Not a Drop Has Passed My Lips

— A Vagrant

There is a saying: "The plan for a day lies in the morning. The plan for a year lies in the spring." Then, "Monday," in the eyes of our countrymen, can of course be regarded as a productive day of the week.

Spring has passed uneventfully, and the morning, too, has slipped away unremarkably in the friction between the soles of our shoes and the pavement. Only "Monday" is out of the ordinary, and contains more painful elements than other days.

Whether spring and morning are unremarkable in the eyes of others, I cannot say! But things like the mundane, the painful, etc., are just my personal feelings!

I am a 21-year-old young office worker who once made a living in a certain industry and has a high school education. Unfortunately, because of its closure, I have been unemployed for nearly a year. But there are still certain reasons that require me to pretend to be a productive member of society. So every day, after getting out of bed, I have to wander the streets to pass the precious – but no longer so precious – morning hours, noon hours... In the evening, this wandering soul can finally say that he has made it through the day. At night, lying in bed and thinking, I feel a bit like a compatriot in distress "unable to return home," tired and in pain. Society! I feel again the depression of having strength but being unable to sell it!

Not long ago, I discovered several public libraries in the city, of which the one in Ximen is more to my liking. In the afternoons, I occasionally take a detour to the Circulation Library to borrow a book to read. There is also the XX Association, which I heard has a rich collection of books, but I was frightened by someone who was ten times colder and more bureaucratic than a clerk and did not dare to visit a second time. Fortunately, the first two are enough to satisfy my desire to read and kill my painful time, and my wandering life can be considered to have come to a small end, and the pain has been relatively reduced. But the problem of selling labor still exists as before, has not been resolved: life is of course still unbearably bitter!

The most painful day for me is every "Monday." On this day, all the places seem to have formed a general alliance to carry out a strike against us "non-capitalists." Early in the morning, I start wandering on Jing'an Temple Road again and have no choice but to walk aimlessly. As for the destination, alas, there is none! In my heart, I just feel the wickedness of people, why not put some benches on the road so that I can rest my tired feet!

The street scene that I used to see still combs through my eyes. Thank goodness! I finally made it to the Huangpu Wharf. Past experience tells me that there is a river, water, and benches for people to rest, and it is also a place where it is relatively easy to pass the time and where I can temporarily forget my pain.

Today has turned to summer weather, and the merciless sun presses on the heads, bodies, and minds of the vagrants... There is not a single thread of peaceful wind in the universe. At this time, the few benches on the dock have already been occupied by quick-footed comrades. At the same time, my feet declare that they want to rest, and my nervous system sends a telegram reporting that my stomach is empty. Ah! The Customs House clock has struck eleven o'clock, and I haven't had a drop of water today! Usually, there is still a desire to read that can overcome hunger, but in this special situation of Monday, hunger is about to stage a counter-offensive.

Alas! The days ahead are long, and the future is really bleak. Finally, I think about it and decide to go to file a report, requesting the gentlemen of society to help me in one or two ways. No matter how big or small the affairs are, as long as there is a position, that will do!
