Movie Special

Little Caesar Edward G. Robinson

— Heng

A Star Who Specializes in Playing Thug Roles

Is Indeed a Gentle and Refined Gentleman

Edward G. Robinson caused a sensation throughout the silver screen after "Little Caesar" was released. From then on, he seemed destined to specialize in playing these "strenuous" roles – the most important of which were gangsters, thugs, etc. He played these roles very deeply and movingly because he was not only a superb thug actor, but also a great and talented actor. People thought that because he played these bad roles, his personality must be similar, but in fact, his character was exactly the opposite of what he played on the screen. He was a gentle and refined gentleman. The fierce light emitted from his dark eyes on the screen could scare the audience so much that their hair stood on end, but usually he was not like that at all. On the set, he was known for being good at worrying. His worries were not unreasonable. He was that way for the sake of the perfection of his work. You see him worrying about the story of his next film, the cast, costumes, set design, etc. He worries about everything.

Before dedicating himself to the silver screen, he was already a famous "red" actor in the United States, and now, of course, it goes without saying. He used to study dramatic art at Columbia University's School of Drama and later received a Master of Arts degree from the school. He also occupies an important position in the New York Theater Guild, the authority on American drama, and he is also proficient in various foreign languages ​​and has performed in several foreign-language theaters. During his sixteen years on the stage, he has performed in many famous stage plays. Although "Little Caesar" was the film that made film audiences deeply aware of his art, he also has many sound film works such as "Five Star Final" and "Two Seconds." He has also acted in many silent films. "Smart Little Girl" was in collaboration with Richard Barthelmess, and "The Sea Lion" was in collaboration with Lionel Barrymore. In this film, he played a farmer, and his performance was powerful and moving, which was really amazing. In fact, he is just as serious and hardworking about every film, which can be proven when we watch his films.

Film Review

Review of "Spring Water and Love Waves"

— Ling He

The Consciousness is Quite Good, the Performance is Excellent

A Rare Production by Mingxing Film Company

Foreword "Chinese films have indeed improved." After watching "Spring Water and Love Waves," I couldn't help but affirm this sentence.

In any case, under the circumstance that European and American films occupy an absolute advantage in the Chinese film market, it is indeed very surprising that Chinese filmmakers can be so energetic to improve their own works, especially the great change in the consciousness of film artists, which makes us somewhat optimistic about the future of Chinese film culture, although this still requires our audience to support it strongly and forcefully.

The above is of course not digressive nonsense.

Zheng Zhengqiu's Three-Anti-ism If we dare not ignore any director's "Idee woroking," then the great change that the elderly Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu has made is indeed worthy of our admiration. He clearly revealed the black幕 of officialdom selling official ranks in China in the picture. He ridiculed these ugly phenomena humorously and painfully in the subtitles. He criticized the frivolous love of those young masters who returned from the United States, explaining the hypocrisy of "love" in the real society (although he still gave him a chance to repent in the end). He explained the conflict in love between people of different wealth. He opposed the tyranny of feudal forces in the countryside and the unreasonableness of patriarchal society. He hated the atrocities of imperialism in semi-colonial China. But in the end, he did not resist strongly, but retreated passively to the northwest to develop "new territories" and was still confused by the fact that "charity" can save the poor masses. Of course, ""new territories" will never be created under the dual oppression, and "charity" has long been not enough to anesthetize people. However, in any case, the "three-anti-ism" that he himself strongly advocated is generally expressed here. At least he has recognized the poison of imperialism, feudal forces, etc. in China. Of course, we don't need to be demanding, so we can be quite satisfied.

Progressive Performance Skills Secondly, we should also pay attention to his directing skills. He narrated the story without any confusion, although he focused on love, he refused to relax the points that must be exposed. Because it is a depiction of love, he made the tone of the play soft. He also paid attention to the lens. Especially the rotating "long shot" of the lake tour is more lively, but because it is an exterior scene and the light is insufficient, it is not beautiful enough. However, several "close-ups" are very wonderful. But even better is the emotional aspect. He made every audience sympathize with Ah Mao and be sad for her, which is very successful in tragedy. But he did not write the Mao Shaojie well enough "bad" so that we don't hate him very much, especially when he repents. This point lacks "contrast" power, but we can't ignore that he is a person who follows the tide. Another point is that the distribution of actor roles is not appropriate. Yan Yuexian is not as suitable for playing Han Qiong. In short, Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu did his duty in terms of performance.

Review of the Performance As for the performance, then Hu Die was quite successful. She was so serious and natural throughout, not at all forced. Her pain and tears were undoubtedly very deep and moving. However, at the end, when Mao Shaojie gave money, she was also so sincere. This is the director's neglect, and it can also be seen that she is not strong enough and has no power to express herself. Wang Xianzai was another success. Tan Zhiyuan has improved slightly compared to before. Hu Ping does not fit the personality. Yan Yuexian is still serious, Zhuan Yiqiu is okay, Li Junqing and Xu Xinyuan are average. Gu Lanjun is not as natural as in "The Future." As for the protagonist Sun Min, he was not successful. A gilded international student is not only gentle and refined. Moreover, there is no change before and after becoming an official. However, the identity of the young master is fairly well expressed.

Epilogue Regarding other points, I think the subtitles are very vivid, but the screening time is too short, and some are simply not completely readable. The photography and scenery are not bad.

In short, I think this is a very mature work of the Mingxing Film Company, and it is naturally rare in Chinese silent films. Roughly, people who care about Chinese films, although not completely satisfied, will not be so disappointed. Finally, I respectfully wish the authors of this film all the best!

New Movie Preview

"Impressions of the Homeless"

— Zhi Zhong

People who escaped from the flood line created by the feudal class and the bloody iron hooves of imperialism to another hunger line are all homeless wanderers. On the other hand, the young wives of capitalists in the city, who are sheltered by imperialism, are abandoned by the playboys who are tired of the old and like the new, and are also wandering aimlessly in the streets. Facts educate them that to survive, they must concentrate their strength and fight.

This kind of realistic subject matter has been seen a lot on the screen, but they are all separate or distorted. Only Yihua Company's debut work "Homeless" closely organizes these three types of typical people—the flood line, the iron hoof line, and the almost abandoned people—and correctly sets out on the dangerous road to struggle. This is a symphony with eight-tone linkages. This is a lifelike sketch of China.

The other day was the screening date for this film. In an office temporarily used as a theater, the screen was displayed on light green plywood. The screenwriter and director Chen Yu explained the plot scene by scene at a rapid pace (because there were no subtitles yet). It wasn't until the bell rang ten times that we left the theater.

My impression of this film is that it breaks the old habit of having a protagonist and supporting actors (in terms of the development of the plot), so that the entire plot is powerfully distributed on each actor. New Montage is used here: In the continuous snow scene, every oppressed person excitedly opens up their way forward in the group will. There are no stars who have been praised here—they are all actors who are on the screen for the first time, but they are all bright lights in the depths of darkness. The light is bright and dark, and he adjusts it appropriately, and we cannot help but admire the superb skills of the Camera Man.

Little Sister Will Star in "Little Sisters"

— Mei Gong

Plus a Group of Smart and Beautiful Little Sisters

Today's movie stars seem to be characters from Liangshan Marsh, with nicknames often topping their names, such as: Frugal Star Chen Yumei, Wild Rose Wang Renmei, Sweetheart Lili Li, Little Actress Yuan Meiyun... etc. Especially famous is Little Sister Li Minghui. She often does not sign her name when writing letters, only writing the three words "Little Sister." It can be seen that she also loves this nickname very much, but she is now a big sister in age. It's just that her temperament is still innocent, lively, and she hasn't changed her true colors as a little sister.

She returned to Shanghai from Hong Kong last year and rejoined the film industry. She starred in the sound film "Pursuit" at Tianyi Company. After it was released, the audience developed a deeper affection for this little sister who had been away from the screen for a long time because she had not lost the lively and innocent style of a little sister from five or six years ago.

She saw that there were many smart and beautiful little sisters in Tianyi Company, such as Yuan Meiyun, Shao Suxia, Chen Qixia, Chen Jingfang, etc., all of whom were fifteen or sixteen years old and had performing talents. If they could gather this group of little stars to co-star in a play, they would definitely achieve complete success. She repeatedly asked Shao Zuiweng to co-star in a film with this group of little sisters. Shao Zuiweng greatly approved of this proposal and planned to write a script specifically for them. The film is called "Little Sisters." The plot is roughly a family drama with educational meaning, starring Little Sister, with Yuan Meiyun, Shao Suxia, Chen Qixia, Chen Jingfang, etc. joining in the co-starring. Once the script is written, filming can begin. It can be said that it is a very interesting thing for Little Sister to star in "Little Sisters."

Tianyi's New Soccer Game Plan

— Jie Bing

The Tianyi football team led by Shao Zuiweng has been practicing morning and evening since its establishment, and all the players have sworn to be loyal and brave. A week ago, Tianyi issued a challenge, sending a letter inviting the News Department team to try out a friendship match at the China Football Field for the first time. Because there were too many fans that day, there was almost no space on the field. It was impossible to stop the game temporarily and agreed to postpone the game. However, the athletes on both sides were ambitious and determined to compete. The News Department had planned repeatedly and prepared two plans to solicit Tianyi's consent. One, hold a temporary secret game to avoid outside attention; Second, the battlefield is located in Yiyuan, sell tickets, and all the proceeds from the sale will be used as donations for "National Salvation Through Aviation." However, it is heard that both parties are currently considering the details and have not formally decided. I don't know when this hilarious soccer game will be staged on the Chun Shenjiang River.

An Overview of Soviet Russian Cinema (1) by Rudolph Messel

— Translated by Bao Han

Editor's Note: Last year, between July and August, the British Fabian Research Bureau organized a Soviet Russian study tour, employing experts to investigate the actual conditions in Soviet Russia, recording the real situation of various national and social undertakings after the Soviet revolution with scientific and professional eyes. Beforehand, the experts had long preparations and discussions in their home country of England, so that after arriving in Soviet Russia, they could immediately engage in the investigation and research within the scope of various selected issues. The result was twelve chapters of highly valuable expert papers, compiled into a book entitled "Twelve Studies in Soviet Russia." Although some experts were prevented from joining the investigation due to other matters, so that aspects such as the equipment of modern medical and health care in Soviet Russia, and the overview of the transportation system, could not be included in the book. However, everything else related to politics, economy, industry, agriculture, real estate, women, children, construction, municipal administration, cultural undertakings, etc., is all-encompassing. In addition, an article of important and profound relevance to this journal is "The Film In Russia" by Rudolph Messel. We have specially invited Mr. Bao Han to translate it for the enjoyment of the readers who support this journal. Furthermore, this book has not been published for long, and there are very few original copies in Shanghai, so its content value is also worthy of cherishing.

(1) Soviet Russian Ideals for Cinema

We who live in Europe are mostly controlled by preconceived notions about drama and film. We view these two forms of performance, firstly, as a means of utilizing someone's or someone's artistic talent, and secondly, as a necessity for our daily entertainment. Now, to understand the real situation of drama or film in Soviet Russia, the first thing to do is to actively eliminate our preconceived notions. We must first have a humble mindset before we can approach the problem, and more importantly, things that we usually consider absolutely immutable are suddenly changed and not absolute, but changeable, in the hands of the Soviet people. At this time, we should try to avoid various disappointments, disillusionments, or even despair. If we can study this topic in this spirit, we can naturally get at least a clear observation, or even understand it; but if we rashly enter this field of right and wrong without this spirit, there is absolutely no possibility of observing any important things, and of course, even less hope of understanding.

In Europe and America, we certainly believe that the biggest reason for the existence of film and theaters is that we, who claim to be a part of the audience, have a need to be entertained. Whether our view is right or wrong, there is no need to debate this here. But here it must be pointed out that this is a view held by the capitalist world, but at the same time it must also be pointed out that this view has completely disappeared in the Soviet Union. (To be continued)
